# STORY_TASKS.md - Story-page Perfection Pass (audit output)

> **Status: SELF-APPROVED, autonomous execution** (per user directive 2026-06-26: "auto accept STORY_TASKS.md and do it autonomous, no need to ask questions till all tasks are done"). See STORY_AUTOPILOT.md for the execution plan and rate-limit pacing.

## How this was produced
- Ultracode audit: 50 per-stage deep audits (narration + on-screen caption/sub/alt + Manim scene + **real extracted frames** + science cross-checked vs technical_report.md/papers), each **adversarially verified**; plus 8 page-level lenses.
- **230 findings** total -> **206 adversarially verified**, **24 unverified** (the consistency, science-global, accessibility-ethics verify steps + the synthesis agent were cut off by the usage cap; their finder output is salvaged here and marked **UNVERIFIED**).
- Severity: **7 blocker / 57 major / 106 minor / 60 polish**.
- Dimensions: A=36, B=21, C=6, D=39, E=26, F=20, G=30, H=13, I=24, J=15  (A=Scientific accuracy; B=Narration<->visual sync; C=Narration quality; D=Animation quality & legibility; E=Pedagogy & completeness; F=Code / UX / interaction; G=Consistency; H=Manim craft; I=Accessibility & ethics; J=Polish)

**Sourcing rule:** every scientific change cites technical_report.md (authoritative for numbers/pipeline) or a paper page. The 51.17->40.63->26.14->18.53 WER ladder is the maker's own work in the report - NOT the 3 papers (those are the foundation).

*From the verified pedagogy-restructure lens.*

**Problem:** Audited merges reclaim 5 slots (covariance 3->2, distillation 3->2, lock cluster 3->2, word-map 2->1, recaps arc+approach 2->1), reinvested into WER-defined-early, audio-crutch honesty, open-vocab lexicon, expanded n-best, corrected foundation credit. Total stays exactly 50.

**Verify note:** Verified by explicit count. The numbered proposed list 1-50 enumerates exactly 50 ids; I diffed it against the current 50-stage array: removed {features-cov, distillation, frozen-recognizer, wfst, sounds-to-words-search, approach} and added {word-map, audio-crutch, open-vocab, reserved-A, reserved-B, reserved-C} = 6 out, 6 in, net 0, total stays 50. Each removal corresponds to a merge I independently confirmed as duplicative (features-cov->grid, distillation->copy-the-teacher, frozen-recognizer->blurry+frozen-lock-how, wfst+sounds->word-map, arc+approach->arc). what-is-wer is MOVED (present in both lists) not added. STAGE_COUNT is derived from STAGES.length and is surfaced as 'XX / 50' in Caption.tsx, so the exactly-50 constraint is real and user-visible. The outline's prose calls items 1-47 a '47-stage spine', but the explicit numbered list ends at 50 with reserved-A/B/C at 48-50, so the deliverable total is unambiguously 50. Every merge is justified. major correct.

**Proposed outline / mapping:**

Adopt the 50-id ordered outline as proposed (hero...end with word-map, audio-crutch, open-vocab inserted, what-is-wer moved before second-opinion, what-is-lm before knobs, cheat before lock, and reserved-A/B/C filling 48-50 with named honesty/depth beats rather than padding).

## TASKS

## BLOCKER (7)

### BLOCKER - A: Scientific accuracy

- **T-A-01 - foundation stage mis-attributes the SPD geometric features (Comstock not a SPD-paper author; McNaughton is)**  _(stage: science-global - UNVERIFIED)_
  - **Wrong:** Both the foundation narration and alt credit "the SPD geometric features" (and the corpus, sensor array, decoder) to "Harshavardhana T. Gowda, with Daniel C. Comstock and Lee M. Miller". This bundles all four foundational contributions under one author trio, but the contributions come from DIFFERENT papers with DIFFERENT author lists. The SPD/geometric-features work is paper 1 "Geometry of orofacial neuromuscular signals", authored by Gowda, McNaughton, Miller — Comstock is NOT an author of it. Daniel C. Comstock is a co-author only of paper 3 "emg2speech" (the General Corpus + ALS participant). McNaughton (the SPD/geometry co-author) is omitted entirely. So the page credits Comstock for geometry work he did not co-author, and drops McNaughton who did.
  - **Fix:** Attribute per contribution rather than as one trio. E.g.: "The corpus and 31-channel array — Gowda, Daniel C. Comstock, and Lee M. Miller (emg2speech). The SPD geometric features — Gowda, Zachary D. McNaughton, and Lee M. Miller. The EMG-to-text decoding framework — Gowda and Lee M. Miller. All from UC Davis." At minimum add McNaughton and do not list Comstock against the SPD features.
  - **Accept:** foundation narration + alt list each foundational contribution with the correct author set from its source paper; McNaughton appears for the SPD/geometry work; Comstock appears only for the corpus/emg2speech work.
  - **Evidence:** stages.ts:419 alt: "the SPD geometric features, and the first EMG-to-text decoder all came out of UC Davis — Harshavardhana T. Gowda, with Daniel C. Comstock and Lee M. Miller."; narration.json:48 foundation: "the credit goes to Harshavardhana Gowda, with Daniel Comstock and Lee Miller." Papers/ PDFs p.1: Paper1 "Geometry..." authors = Gowda, Zachary D. McNaughton, Lee M. Miller (SPD manifold features); Paper3 "emg2speech" authors = Gowda, Daniel C. Comstock, Lee M. Miller (corpus + ALS). Paper2 "Non-invasive...geometric perspective" authors = Gowda, Miller (EMG-to-text/SPD/silent/single subject).
  - **Verified:** _UNVERIFIED - adversarial verify was rate-limited; confirm against source before applying._

### BLOCKER - B: Narration<->visual sync

- **T-B-01 - Blank-penalty dial visibly INCREASES the WER meter (18% to 61%), contradicting the 'biggest lever' punchline**  _(stage: knobs - verified)_
  - **Wrong:** A single shared WER meter is driven through two incompatible measurement regimes. Beat 3 drops it to 18% (tuned/final regime) and it HOLDS at 18% through the whole blank story. Beat 5 silently resets the same meter to 78% (untuned val[:200] @ scale 1.0 regime) and drops it to 61%. On screen the viewer sees 18% -> (jump up) 78% -> 61% as the blank dial is turned UP toward its tuned 2.0 value, directly under the punchline 'blank penalty - the single biggest lever.' A scientist or layperson reads this as: the beneficial dial made the error rate ~3-4x worse. Nothing on screen signals the regime/dataset switch.
  - **Fix:** Never share one WER meter across two regimes. Either give the blank dial its own clearly-scoped mini-meter ('blank 0->2 on a held slice: 78->61'), or start the blank demo from the pre-tuned ~76% and show a DROP to ~61% (never from 18%), or freeze the main meter and animate only bars + a labelled delta. The on-screen error indicator must never rise when a beneficial dial is turned toward its tuned value.
  - **Accept:** Scrubbing beats 3->5, the on-screen error indicator never increases when a beneficial dial is turned toward its tuned value; 'biggest lever' is supported by a visible DROP or an explicitly regime-scoped separate meter.
  - **Evidence:** s20_knobs.py line 169 wer_t=ValueTracker(0.76); line 206 wer_t->0.18 (beat3); line 264 `wer_t.set_value(0.78) # frame the blank lever as the big 78 -> 61 drop` (silent reset); line 276 wer_t->0.61; punchline line 302 'blank penalty - the single biggest lever' at WER_Y+0.78 (directly above the 61% meter). Report lines 75-76: 77.6->60.6 is val[:200] AT scale 1.0 (untuned); the 18.53/18% is the tuned final regime.
  - **Verified:** Refutation attempt FAILED - this is real and severe. Frame at 9.0s (blank penalty still 0.0): meter reads '18% wrong', fill bar short (~1/4 width). Frame at 11.8s/end (blank penalty 2.0): meter reads '61% wrong', fill bar >half width, with 'the single biggest lever' punchline above it. So the meter visibly rises when the 'good' dial is turned up. Code comment at line 264 literally admits the reset intent. Blocker severity is correct: for a science-rigorous audience this directly inverts the claim. Compounding harm: even taken at face value the scale dial dropped 58 pts (76->18) vs blank's 17 pts (78->61), so the meter also undercuts 'blank is the single biggest lever' - that compounding is a downstream symptom of this same shared-meter defect, not a separate bug.

### BLOCKER - E: Pedagogy & completeness

- **T-E-01 - The 'frozen lock' is stated (30) BEFORE the cheat it solves is explained (31), then re-taught (32)**  _(stage: pedagogy-restructure - verified)_
  - **Wrong:** frozen-recognizer (30) asserts the locked-reader fix FIRST. blurry-average-cheat (31) only then explains the blur-to-midpoint cheat the lock defeats. frozen-lock-how (32) re-explains the lock again. Reader gets the solution before the problem, then the problem, then the solution again.
  - **Fix:** Reorder to cause-then-cure and merge the two lock stages: (1) blurry-average-cheat = the cheat, (2) frozen-lock-how = the single fix. Delete frozen-recognizer (its content is the union of 31+32). Net -1, cause now precedes cure.
  - **Accept:** On-page order is cheat THEN lock; exactly one stage explains the frozen recognizer; nothing states the lock before the stage that introduces the blur cheat.
  - **Evidence:** stages.ts L312-329. Array order: frozen-recognizer(30) 'A locked reader forces the copy to actually spell out sounds' -> blurry-average-cheat(31) 'Why lock a reader onto the copy? Because just be close has a cheat' -> frozen-lock-how(32) 'The fix: a locked sound-reader'. narration: frozen-recognizer and frozen-lock-how both 'bolt on a sound-reader and freeze it.'
  - **Verified:** Confirmed and severity upheld. Order verified: frozen-recognizer=30, blurry-average-cheat=31, frozen-lock-how=32. frozen-recognizer narration introduces the s/z midpoint cheat AND the frozen reader fix together ('bolt on a sound-reader and freeze it'). blurry-average-cheat narration THEN re-introduces the same midpoint cheat from scratch ('What's the laziest way to stay close to both at once? Plant one point dead in the middle'). frozen-lock-how narration THEN re-introduces the same fix ('you bolt this sound-reader on and freeze it solid'). So the full cheat+fix is taught at 30, the cheat alone re-taught at 31, the fix alone re-taught at 32 — a solution-before-problem inversion plus triple coverage. blocker is defensible: this is not mere redundancy but an ordering inversion that breaks comprehension (reader is handed the cure before ever seeing the disease). Note distillation(29) also seeds the same cheat/fix, so the idea spans 29-32.

### BLOCKER - F: Code / UX / interaction

- **T-F-01 - Subtitles DEFAULT ON requirement is not met (narrationOn defaults false; unreachable under reduced motion)**  _(stage: code-ux - verified)_
  - **Wrong:** Signed-off A11y rule is 'narration subtitles DEFAULT ON'. Subtitles render only when on = narrationOn (Subtitles.tsx:49,110); narrationOn defaults false (useStore.ts:58) and is flipped true ONLY in PlayButton.start() (PlayButton.tsx:129), which lives in the control bar that is display:none under prefers-reduced-motion (PlayButton.module.css:114-118). So reduced-motion users can never turn subtitles on, and everyone else gets them OFF until they press Play. Captions are also aria-hidden (Subtitles.tsx:114).
  - **Fix:** Add a `subtitlesOn` flag defaulting true, render Subtitles whenever a clip is active independent of audio; keep the speaker control for AUDIO only; expose captions to AT (drop aria-hidden / polite live region); persist preference.
  - **Accept:** On first load with defaults, scrubbing/playing any narrated stage shows the word-synced subtitle band; a reduced-motion user can read captions; toggling audio off does not hide subtitles.
  - **Evidence:** useStore.ts:58 (narrationOn: false); Subtitles.tsx:49 (on = narrationOn), :110 (if (!on...) return null), :114 (aria-hidden); PlayButton.tsx:129 (setNarrationOn(true) only here); PlayButton.module.css:114-118 (bar display:none for reduced-motion)
  - **Verified:** CONFIRMED and solid. Grepped src/store — there is NO separate subtitle flag; Subtitles.tsx line 49 reads narrationOn directly and line 110 early-returns null when off. useStore.ts:58 confirms narrationOn:false default. The ONLY setNarrationOn(true) call is PlayButton.tsx:129 inside start(). PlayButton.module.css:114-118 hides the entire .bar under reduced-motion, so that setter is unreachable there. This directly violates the signed-off 'narration subtitles DEFAULT ON' A11y rule. Blocker is the correct severity for a signed-off-rule violation that also leaves reduced-motion users with no caption path.

### BLOCKER - G: Consistency

- **T-G-01 - Bare digits in narration break TTS spell-out rule (features-window, knobs)**  _(stage: consistency - UNVERIFIED)_
  - **Wrong:** Narration must spell out all numbers/units for the TTS voice (en-US-AvaMultilingualNeural), and the file already does this everywhere else (e.g. 'eighteen and a half', 'twenty point nine', 'five thousand times a second', 'fifty snapshots'). But two entries leave raw digits that Ava will mispronounce or read inconsistently.
  - **Fix:** Spell out: features-window -> "thirty-one wiggly traces", "twenty-five milliseconds wide", "only twenty milliseconds", "shares five milliseconds". knobs -> "near zero point two five" and "near two point zero". Match the spelled-out convention used in signal/binding-constraint/arc.
  - **Accept:** grep -P '[0-9]' narration.json returns no bare cardinal/decimal numbers in any value (all spelled out); TTS re-render of features-window and knobs pronounces every quantity correctly.
  - **Evidence:** narration.json line 8 features-window: "31 wiggly traces", "25 milliseconds wide", "only 20 milliseconds", "shares 5 milliseconds". narration.json line 38 knobs: "turn it down near 0.25", "on blank, near 2.0". Contrast line 7 signal which spells "thirty-one" and line 43 which spells "twenty point nine"/"eighteen and a half".
  - **Verified:** _UNVERIFIED - adversarial verify was rate-limited; confirm against source before applying._

### BLOCKER - I: Accessibility & ethics

- **T-I-01 - Foundation stage misattributes SPD/geometric features and credits wrong author set**  _(stage: accessibility-ethics - UNVERIFIED)_
  - **Wrong:** The foundation stage credits 'the SPD geometric features, and the first EMG-to-text decoder' to 'Harshavardhana T. Gowda, with Daniel C. Comstock and Lee M. Miller.' But the SPD/geometric-features work is paper 1 'Geometry of orofacial...' (Gowda, Zachary D. McNaughton, Lee M. Miller) and paper 2 'Non-invasive...a geometric perspective' (Gowda, Miller). Daniel C. Comstock is an author of paper 3 (the emg2speech corpus/ALS paper), NOT the geometry papers. So the credit (a) omits McNaughton entirely and (b) attaches Comstock to a contribution he is not on. The corpus credit is right (Comstock = paper 3) but the geometry credit is wrong.
  - **Fix:** Split the credit by contribution: attribute the SPD/geometric features + first non-invasive EMG-to-text decoding to Gowda, McNaughton (geometry paper) and Gowda, Miller (geometric-perspective paper); attribute the 31-channel General Corpus to Gowda, Comstock, Miller (emg2speech). Either name all four UC Davis authors (Gowda, McNaughton, Comstock, Miller) on the foundation plate, or use two lines mapping each foundation stone to its real author set. Update both stages.ts:418-419 and narration.json 'foundation'. Re-render the foundation clip + .captions.json/.mp3 to match (TTS must spell 'McNaughton').
  - **Accept:** Foundation alt, sub, narration text, on-screen name plate, captions.json and mp3 all name McNaughton for the geometry/SPD contribution and do not credit Comstock for SPD; corpus stays credited to Comstock. An ASR/EMG expert reading the credits cannot find an author attached to a paper they did not co-author.
  - **Evidence:** stages.ts:418-419 alt+sub ('the SPD geometric features, and the first EMG-to-text decoder all came out of UC Davis — Harshavardhana T. Gowda, with Daniel C. Comstock and Lee M. Miller'); narration.json line 48 'foundation' repeats the same author set; paper 1 title page authors = 'Harshavardhana T. Gowda, Zachary D. McNaughton, Lee M. Miller' (SPD manifold + 16-subject open dataset); paper 2 title page authors = 'Harshavardhana T. Gowda and Lee M. Miller' (SPD, EMG-to-text); paper 3 title page authors = 'Harshavardhana T. Gowda, Daniel C. Comstock, and Lee M. Miller' (the General/ALS corpus).
  - **Verified:** _UNVERIFIED - adversarial verify was rate-limited; confirm against source before applying._
- **T-I-02 - Narration subtitles are aria-hidden and unavailable unless Play is pressed — fails default-on + WCAG**  _(stage: accessibility-ethics - UNVERIFIED)_
  - **Wrong:** USER-SIGNED-OFF A11Y rule: 'narration subtitles DEFAULT ON.' In practice: (1) the Subtitles overlay carries aria-hidden="true", so screen-reader users get no access to the spoken narration text at all; (2) Subtitles render only while narrationOn && playing, and narrationOn defaults to false (only auto-armed on Play), so a user who reads by scrolling (never pressing Play) never sees the narration transcript — they only get the much shorter on-screen 'sub' abstract, which is itself hidden during Play. There is no native <track kind="subtitles"> and no persistent 'captions on' preference. So subtitles are neither default-on for the scroll path nor exposed to assistive tech. This is both a WCAG 1.2.2/1.2.4 (captions for media) gap and a violation of the signed-off requirement.
  - **Fix:** Make captions a first-class, default-on, accessible track: (a) remove aria-hidden from the Subtitles wrap (or render the active sentence in an aria-live=polite region) so it is announced; (b) decouple subtitle display from the audio-armed state — show captions whenever the story is being read (scroll OR play), driven by stage/local-progress timing, not only when audio plays; (c) add a persistent 'captions on' store flag defaulting to true with a visible toggle in the control bar; (d) ensure the full narration.json text is reachable as DOM text for screen readers even with audio off.
  - **Accept:** With audio off and using only scroll, the narration text appears on screen by default; a screen reader can read the active narration sentence; a visible captions toggle exists and persists; aria-hidden no longer suppresses the subtitle text from AT. Verified on a real screen reader (VoiceOver) reading the narration of at least the hero + one Act-2 stage.
  - **Evidence:** Subtitles.tsx:114 '<div className={styles.wrap} aria-hidden="true">'; Subtitles.tsx:110 'if (!on || cueIdx < 0 ...) return null' where on = narrationOn; useStore.ts:55 'narrationOn: false'; PlayButton.tsx:129 'setNarrationOn(true)' only fires on Play; Caption.tsx:68 sub is rendered only when '!captionsMode' (hidden during play); no '<track' element exists (grep returned none); narration.json carries the full spoken text but is never surfaced as accessible text.
  - **Verified:** _UNVERIFIED - adversarial verify was rate-limited; confirm against source before applying._

## MAJOR (57)

### MAJOR - A: Scientific accuracy

- **T-A-02 - "seven-billion-word language model" is factually wrong (parameters, not words)**  _(stage: approach - verified)_
  - **Wrong:** Narration calls the reranker "a seven-billion-word language model." Qwen2.5-7B-Instruct has 7 billion PARAMETERS, not words; a 7B model is trained on trillions of tokens and has no fixed word count. The sibling rerank stage deliberately phrases it correctly as "a language model with seven billion learned patterns," so this is also an internal inconsistency. I downgrade from blocker to major: it is a genuine factual error an ML reader will flag and worth fixing, but it sits in an explanatory beat, the conveyed meaning (a large LLM) survives, and the on-screen chip already reads the correct "7B rerank" — it does not break the page or fundamentally mislead about the science.
  - **Fix:** Replace "a seven-billion-word language model" with the rerank stage's already-validated phrasing, e.g. "a language model with seven billion learned patterns." Keep the on-screen "7B rerank" chip.
  - **Accept:** Narration no longer equates the 7B model with a word count; phrasing matches the rerank stage; re-rendered TTS audio updated.
  - **Evidence:** narration.json line 46 (approach): "...let a seven-billion-word language model pick the best line." narration.json line 42 (rerank): "a language model with seven billion learned patterns". technical_report.md line 160: "Qwen2.5-7B-Instruct" with QLoRA (4-bit nf4 + LoRA r=16) — a 7B-parameter model.
  - **Verified:** Verified narration.json line 46 contains "seven-billion-word language model" and line 42 contains "seven billion learned patterns" (the corrected sibling phrasing). technical_report.md line 160 confirms the model is Qwen2.5-7B-Instruct, a 7B-PARAMETER model. Frame at 8.0s shows the on-screen chip reads "7B rerank" (correct), so only the spoken word is wrong. Severity corrected blocker->major: real factual error but non-page-breaking, meaning preserved, display already correct.
- **T-A-03 - Move 1 framed as "opened it to a full dictionary" — the baseline was ALREADY open-vocabulary**  _(stage: approach - verified)_
  - **Wrong:** Move 1 narration says "we re-tuned the decode and opened it to a full dictionary, so it can spell words it never trained on." The 51.17->40.63 gain came from recovering missing decode-time hyperparameters (acoustic scale, blank penalty, regenerated words.txt, checkpoint selection) on the SAME open-vocabulary HLG graph the original authors already used. The open-vocab / full-dictionary capability existed in the baseline; the report states the gain is "attributable to a correctly specified open-vocabulary decode, not to any model change." Claiming the project "opened it to a full dictionary" overstates the contribution and mis-describes the mechanism — a credit/accuracy issue experts scrutinize.
  - **Fix:** Reframe move 1 to the true story: it was already open-vocabulary; we recovered the decode settings the public release omitted (acoustic scale + blank penalty + words.txt + checkpoint selection). E.g. "One: we recovered the decode settings the original release left out — the right acoustic scale and blank penalty — and a third of the errors vanished."
  - **Accept:** Move-1 narration no longer credits this project with adding open-vocabulary / a full dictionary; it attributes the gain to recovered decode hyperparameters, consistent with report section 3.
  - **Evidence:** narration.json line 46: "we re-tuned the decode and opened it to a full dictionary." technical_report.md line 6: "recover the missing open-vocabulary decode hyperparameters"; line 69: HLG "...the same graph the authors use"; lines 73-80: missing pieces are acoustic scale, blank penalty, words.txt, checkpoint; line 92: WER gain "attributable to a correctly specified open-vocabulary decode, not to any model change."
  - **Verified:** Independently verified against technical_report.md: line 5-6 ("recover the missing open-vocabulary decode hyperparameters"), line 69 ("the same graph the authors use"), line 92 ("not to any model change"). The report is unambiguous the baseline was already open-vocabulary and the gain was decode-hyperparameter recovery, not adding a dictionary. Confirmed real; major is correct because it overstates the project's contribution in a beat that experts will check against the report.
- **T-A-04 - Narration says each reader is wrong "a fifth of the time" but each model is ~26%, contradicting the screen and the next sentence**  _(stage: ensemble-nbest - verified)_
  - **Wrong:** Narration sentence 1 says each reader "hands you one sentence that's wrong about a fifth of the time" (a fifth = 20%). But each individual reader is ~26.14% WER; ~20% is the result AFTER averaging the two. Sentence 3 then says averaging takes you "from twenty-six percent wrong down to about twenty" — so it simultaneously claims each reader is 20% (sent.1) and 26% (sent.3). The on-screen ruler parks the marker at 26% as each reader's starting state.
  - **Fix:** Change "wrong about a fifth of the time" to "wrong about a quarter of the time" so each reader's ~26% matches the on-screen 26% and the 26→20 averaging drop becomes coherent.
  - **Accept:** Per-reader error fraction in narration equals the 26% shown at BEAT 1 and is strictly worse than the post-average ~20%; sentences 1 and 3 no longer contradict.
  - **Evidence:** narration.json key "ensemble-nbest": "...each hands you one sentence that's wrong about a fifth of the time" vs "...nudges you from twenty-six percent wrong down to about twenty." technical_report.md line 149: "Ensembling alone: 26.14 → ~20.1 WER" (each model 26.14, average ~20.1). stages.ts line 369 alt correctly says "Two readers average to about 20% wrong". Frame v_0.12 (BEAT 1): WER marker labeled "26%" under reader A/B curves.
  - **Verified:** Independently confirmed: report line 149 says each model is 26.14 and the average is ~20.1; frame v_0.12 shows the ruler marker labeled "26%" while both reader curves are present, so "a fifth" (20%) for a single reader contradicts both the visible 26% and sentence 3's own "twenty-six percent". Real factual+coherence error; major is correct.
- **T-A-05 - "First EMG-to-text decoder" is an over-claim Gowda's own papers contradict**  _(stage: foundation - verified)_
  - **Wrong:** Narration and the stages.ts alt both credit UC Davis with "the first EMG-to-text decoder." This claims primacy that the cited papers themselves refute: Gaddy & Klein (2020 EMNLP, 2021) published EMG silent-speech-to-text years earlier, and both the geometric-perspective and emg2speech papers cite them as the prior EMG-to-text/speech benchmark. Severity corrected from blocker to major: it is a real, sensitive (credit-beat) factual error, but it is confined to one word ("first") in the audio narration + alt text, and the on-screen visual is already correct, so there is no layout/functional break.
  - **Fix:** Drop "first." In narration replace "the first E M G to text decoder" with "their E M G to text decoder"; in stages.ts alt replace "the first EMG-to-text decoder" with "the EMG-to-text decoder we build on," matching the on-screen stone wording.
  - **Accept:** Neither narration nor alt claims primacy ("first"); the spoken/alt wording matches the on-screen stones, which never say "first."
  - **Evidence:** narration.json "foundation": "...the first E M G to text decoder — every one of those came out of U C Davis."; stages.ts line 419 alt: "and the first EMG-to-text decoder all came out of UC Davis". The on-screen left stone instead says only "EMG → text at the phoneme level" (frame fnd_4.76_v.jpg), never "first."
  - **Verified:** Independently proven. papers/Non-invasive...geometric perspective.pdf Section 2 Prior work: 'The current benchmark for silent speech interfaces is established by Gaddy and Klein (2020, 2021)' and 'Unlike prior EMG-to-speech systems (Gaddy and Klein, 2020, 2021; Benster et al., 2024)...'. emg2speech.pdf p.1: 'EMG-to-speech (Gaddy and Klein, 2020, 2021)' and reports Gaddy&Klein 2020 WER 68%, 2021 42% — text WERs, i.e. EMG-to-text predating Gowda. Claim is false; severity downgraded blocker->major because impact is one word in audio/alt only, visual already correct.
- **T-A-06 - Acoustic-scale dial alone shown taking WER 76% to 18% - over-attributes the full pipeline to one decode knob**  _(stage: knobs - verified)_
  - **Wrong:** Beat 3 moves only the acoustic-scale needle (1.0 -> 0.25) and the meter falls 76% -> 18%. But 18.53 is the FINAL full-pipeline result (bidirectional Conformer + 4-term distillation + 2-model ensemble + n-best union + LIFT reranker). Scale tuning alone on the Conformer reaches 26.14, and on the TDS baseline corrected decode reaches 40.63 - not 18. Pinning the acoustic-scale needle to an 18% readout tells an ML viewer that one decode hyperparameter buys the entire ~58-point reduction.
  - **Fix:** Decouple the meter from the modeling wins: label it illustrative/relative ('words snap into place') or use an honest scale-only delta (~75% -> 'words become legible'), and reserve the 18.53 headline for the ensemble/rerank stages where it is earned.
  - **Accept:** No single-dial move on this stage displays a WER number that is actually the product of the full ensemble+rerank pipeline; the scale lever's on-screen effect matches what decode tuning alone achieves per the report.
  - **Evidence:** s20_knobs.py lines 205-206: only scale_t (1.0->0.25) and wer_t (0.76->0.18) move. Report: stage 2 Conformer (scale 0.25) = 26.14 (line 27/132); stage 3 final ensemble+rerank = 18.53 (line 28/35); baseline corrected decode = 40.63 (line 88); line 226 '0.25/2.0' is the Conformer decode config applied on top of the full model.
  - **Verified:** Refutation attempt FAILED - confirmed via report table (lines 26-28): 18.53 is stage 3 (final ensemble+n-best union+LIFT), 26.14 is the Conformer at scale 0.25, 40.63 is the baseline corrected decode. The scene maps scale->0.25 to 18%, which is the full-pipeline number, not any scale-only result. Major severity is right: it is an accuracy/over-claim defect for the science audience, distinct from B (B is the visible rise; A is the single-knob attribution of the headline number).
- **T-A-07 - Masseter described as opening the mouth — it only closes it**  _(stage: muscles - verified)_
  - **Wrong:** Narration and the on-screen callout claim the masseter "opens and closes your mouth." Anatomically the masseter is purely a jaw elevator (closer) — the prime mover of the bite/clench. Mouth opening is driven by the lateral pterygoid, digastric/suprahyoid muscles and gravity, not the masseter. The error appears in voice, on-screen sub, AND default-on subtitles.
  - **Fix:** Voice: "...the masseter, the slab over your jaw, clamps it shut" or "powers the bite that closes your mouth"; sub: "jaw · clenches" or "jaw · closes". Keep the masseter as a closer only.
  - **Accept:** Neither narration, the on-screen masseter sub, nor the subtitle track claims the masseter opens the mouth; it is described as a jaw closer/elevator only.
  - **Evidence:** narration.json key "muscles": "...the masseter, the slab over your jaw, opens and closes your mouth."; i5_muscles.py:101 callout(... 'masseter', 'jaw · open/close' ...); public/anim/muscles.captions.json carries the same spoken text ("masseter" caption at t=17).
  - **Verified:** Verified textbook anatomy: masseter is one of four muscles of mastication, an unambiguous mandibular elevator with no jaw-opening action. Error is real and triplicated (voice/sub/caption). I DOWNGRADE the auditor's 'blocker' to 'major': it is an isolated factual error in a flavor/explanatory beat, not page-breaking and not a misrepresentation of the project's own results — but it is flatly wrong and trivially falsifiable by the science-literate target audience, so it is a genuine credibility defect that must be fixed.
- **T-A-08 - Sternohyoid mis-credited as the muscle that "sets your pitch"**  _(stage: muscles - verified)_
  - **Wrong:** Narration says "low in the throat the sternohyoid sets your pitch" and the sub reads "larynx · pitch." The sternohyoid is an infrahyoid strap muscle that depresses the hyoid/larynx. Vocal pitch (F0) is set primarily by the cricothyroid and vocal-fold tension via the vagus/recurrent laryngeal nerve; the sternohyoid only contributes to laryngeal height/positioning, not pitch control.
  - **Fix:** Voice: "...low in the throat strap muscles like the sternohyoid steady your larynx"; sub: "larynx · holds steady". (A true pitch muscle would be the cricothyroid, but it is intrinsic and not surface-EMG-friendly.)
  - **Accept:** The sternohyoid is no longer described as setting pitch; it is given its real laryngeal-positioning role (or a correct pitch muscle is named).
  - **Evidence:** narration.json key "muscles": "...low in the throat the sternohyoid sets your pitch."; i5_muscles.py:109 callout(... 'sternohyoid', 'larynx · pitch' ...); muscles.captions.json caption "sternohyoid" at t=25.
  - **Verified:** Confirmed at major. Standard laryngeal physiology: F0 is controlled by intrinsic muscles (cricothyroid primary), not the infrahyoid strap muscles. "Sets your pitch" is wrong enough to draw an objection from a voice/speech scientist — the explicitly scrutinized audience per the taste decisions. Same triplication (voice/sub/caption) as the masseter error. Severity 'major' is correct.
- **T-A-09 - "first EMG-to-text decoder" over-claims; the source papers cite Gaddy & Klein as prior EMG work**  _(stage: science-global - UNVERIFIED)_
  - **Wrong:** The foundation alt calls it "the first EMG-to-text decoder." The UC Davis papers themselves do NOT claim primacy of EMG decoding — paper 2 explicitly frames its novelty as direct EMG-to-TEXT (vs prior EMG-to-audio) and cites Gaddy & Klein (2020, 2021) and Défossez et al. (2023) as prior EMG/silent-speech work. Calling it the "first EMG-to-text decoder" full stop overstates and risks expert pushback, since earlier EMG silent-speech decoders exist; the genuine novelty is the SPD-geometric, alignment-free, direct EMG-to-text framing on this corpus.
  - **Fix:** Soften to what the papers actually claim, e.g. "the first direct, alignment-free EMG-to-text decoder on this corpus" or simply "the EMG-to-text decoding framework" — drop the unqualified "first."
  - **Accept:** No unqualified "first EMG-to-text decoder" claim remains; wording matches the papers' own framing (direct EMG-to-text / concrete baseline), avoiding primacy over Gaddy & Klein.
  - **Evidence:** stages.ts:419 alt: "...and the first EMG-to-text decoder all came out of UC Davis". Paper2 PDF: "In contrast to prior approaches (Défossez et al., 2023; Gaddy and Klein, 2020, 2021), which learn representations by mapping time-aligned ... signals to corresponding audio, we ..." and "Unlike prior EMG-to-speech benchmarks (Gaddy and Klein, 2020, 2021)...". Paper2 only claims "strong evidence that direct EMG-to-text transcription is feasible" + "establish a concrete baseline", not a first.
  - **Verified:** _UNVERIFIED - adversarial verify was rate-limited; confirm against source before applying._
- **T-A-10 - HuBERT/self-supervised "thousands of hours of audio" overstates LibriSpeech 960h**  _(stage: science-global - UNVERIFIED)_
  - **Wrong:** Two places say the 100 units / self-supervised model was trained on "thousands of hours of audio." The 100 HuBERT units are trained self-supervised on LibriSpeech 960h — i.e. just under one thousand hours, not "thousands." "Thousands of hours" is a factual overstatement. The narration's softer "endless plain audio" (where-units-from) is fine, but the stages.ts alt/sub assert a specific quantity that is wrong.
  - **Fix:** Replace "thousands of hours" with "hundreds of hours" or "about a thousand hours" (or keep it vague: "a huge pile of plain audio"). Apply to both targets-units and where-units-from.
  - **Accept:** Neither stage claims "thousands of hours"; the figure is consistent with LibriSpeech 960h or left appropriately vague.
  - **Evidence:** stages.ts:226 sub (targets-units): "100 sound-shapes a model discovered on its own from thousands of hours of audio"; stages.ts:232 sub (where-units-from): "play a model thousands of hours of audio". Report references HuBERT [7] (Hsu et al.); HuBERT Base is trained on LibriSpeech 960h (≈ one thousand hours, not thousands). Fact sheet flags this as likely OVER-stating.
  - **Verified:** _UNVERIFIED - adversarial verify was rate-limited; confirm against source before applying._
- **T-A-11 - Augmentation list is largely invented; report names only jitter, dropout, and an audio-teacher KL**  _(stage: twin-warmstart - verified)_
  - **Wrong:** The authoritative report Section 5.1 describes the second ensembled model's augmentation as exactly "stronger jitter/dropout" plus a "BiLSTM audio-teacher frame-KL". The scene and narration assert four specific corruptions — time-masking, gentle noise, frame rotation — none of which appear anywhere in the report. "frame rotation" is a strong, specific SPD-manifold claim with no source. An ML reader checking the report will see fabricated method detail.
  - **Fix:** Replace the invented list with what the report supports: "stronger jitter and dropout" (optionally the audio-teacher as a separate help term). If a vivid longer list is wanted, keep it generic ("we corrupt its inputs harder") rather than naming operations the report does not perform.
  - **Accept:** Every named augmentation in caption/sub/alt/narration/scene maps to a knob actually present in technical_report.md Section 5.1 (jitter, dropout); no unsourced operation (rotation, time-masking, added noise) is presented as fact.
  - **Evidence:** technical_report.md:148 "p2": stronger jitter/dropout, BiLSTM audio-teacher frame-KL; :62 EpochJitter augmentation. grep across the report for rotat|mask|noise|SpecAug returns no augmented-model hit (the only "masked" at line 117 is the L2 feature-regression distillation term, unrelated). Scene :270-271 and narration add time-masking, gentle noise, frame rotation.
  - **Verified:** Verified by reading report lines 146-151 directly: Section 5.1 augmentation = jitter/dropout + audio-teacher frame-KL only. grep for rotat|mask|noise|SpecAug confirms none of time-masking/gentle-noise/frame-rotation exist for the augmented model. The fabricated terms appear verbatim in scene line 270-271 and narration. Severity major is correct: this is invented method detail in a science-facing asset, and "frame rotation" on an SPD covariance manifold is a particularly specific false claim.

### MAJOR - E: Pedagogy & completeness

- **T-E-02 - Local redundancy: three consecutive stages re-run the same blur-problem / locked-reader loop**  _(stage: blurry-average-cheat - verified)_
  - **Wrong:** frozen-recognizer (stage 29), blurry-average-cheat (stage 30), and frozen-lock-how (stage 31) overlap heavily: frozen-recognizer narration states BOTH the problem and the fix; blurry-average-cheat re-expands the problem; frozen-lock-how re-expands the fix. The blurry-average-cheat caption asks 'Why lock a reader onto the copy?' but the locked reader was already introduced one stage earlier, so the motivating question arrives after its own answer.
  - **Fix:** Reorder so problem fully precedes fix: blurry-average-cheat (problem) before the lock stages, and collapse the fix into a single stage rather than splitting it across frozen-recognizer + frozen-lock-how. Trim frozen-recognizer to a one-line bridge or merge it into frozen-lock-how. Flag for outline sign-off; keep 50-stage total.
  - **Accept:** Each of the three adjacent stages states something the others do not; the 'why lock a reader' question is not answered before it is asked; no two adjacent stages both depict 'two sounds blur into one, then a padlocked reader splits them apart'.
  - **Evidence:** stages.ts:314 frozen-recognizer caption 'A locked reader forces the copy to actually spell out sounds'; stages.ts:315 alt 'Two different sounds collapse into one blurry vector, then a padlocked phoneme reader forces them apart'; stages.ts:320 blurry-average-cheat caption 'Why lock a reader onto the copy? Because "just be close" has a cheat'; stages.ts:326-328 frozen-lock-how re-presents the fix. narration.json:31 (frozen-recognizer) already gives problem+fix ('land halfway... bolt on a sound-reader and freeze it'); narration.json:32 re-tells the problem; narration.json:33 re-tells the fix.
  - **Verified:** Independently confirmed by reading stages.ts:312-329 and narration.json:31-33. frozen-recognizer narration (line 31) genuinely contains the full problem+fix arc ('land halfway between them' + 'bolt on a sound-reader and freeze it'), so blurry-average-cheat and frozen-lock-how are expansions of material already delivered. The question-after-answer ordering (caption line 320 vs the locked-reader already shown at line 314) is real. Major is appropriate: this is a structural/editorial defect a careful reviewer notices, flagged for outline sign-off, not a hard render bug.

### MAJOR - F: Code / UX / interaction

- **T-F-02 - Narration→scrub drift: audio time mapped linearly to scroll while clip beats are uneven**  _(stage: code-ux - verified)_
  - **Wrong:** PlayButton sets scroll = rect.top + (narration.time/narration.duration)*rect.height (linear in audio time). MediaLayer independently scrubs the video to local*video.duration (linear in scroll). Both are linear, but neither the Manim clip's visual beats nor the spoken sentence boundaries (captions.json cue.t) are evenly spaced, so the visible beat lags/leads the spoken sentence by a variable amount across a 165vh section.
  - **Fix:** Introduce per-stage beat anchors mapping cue.t boundaries → local scroll position (→ clip currentTime); piecewise-linear interpolate between anchors instead of one global ratio.
  - **Accept:** For each narrated stage, the on-screen beat a sentence describes is visible within ~150ms of that sentence being spoken, verified by stepping through cue boundaries.
  - **Evidence:** PlayButton.tsx:84-85 (p = narration.time/narration.duration; scrollTo rect.top + p*rect.height, linear); MediaLayer.tsx:131-132 (t = local*video.duration, linear in scroll); alignment-problem.captions.json verified non-uniform
  - **Verified:** CONFIRMED. PlayButton.tsx:84 `const p = clamp01(narration.time / narration.duration)` then line 85 scrolls rect.top + p*rect.height — purely linear in audio time. MediaLayer.tsx:131 `const t = local * video.duration` — purely linear in scroll. Ran node on public/anim/alignment-problem.captions.json: 9 cues; cue0 words at t = 0.08, 0.205, 0.409, 0.489, 0.966 (clearly non-uniform), cue1 starts 3.239. Two independent linear maps over non-uniform beats is a real drift source. Severity major (medium confidence) is correct — it is a perceptible sync defect, not a crash.
- **T-F-03 - 50 simultaneous <video> + 50 <audio> elements: compositor and decoder pressure**  _(stage: code-ux - verified)_
  - **Wrong:** All 50 stages are act2 (video), so MediaLayer mounts 50 <video preload='auto'> and NarrationLayer mounts 50 <audio preload='auto'>. Far stages are display:none and src is only set within ±2/±1 of active (good mitigation), but 50 <video> nodes still exist; on Safari/iOS preload='auto' plus repeated currentTime seeking is a known memory/decoder-exhaustion path, and toggling display back from none forces re-decode and can flash.
  - **Fix:** Set preload='none'/'metadata' outside the active window and 'auto' only near active; virtualize so only ~5 <video>/<audio> nodes exist at once (keyed by active index).
  - **Accept:** On iOS Safari, scrubbing the full story does not hit the decoder/memory ceiling (no blanked clips); the DOM holds a bounded number of media elements regardless of stage count.
  - **Evidence:** stages.ts: 50 act2() stage instances verified (node count), each media.kind==='video'; MediaLayer.tsx:39-44 VIDEO_STAGES = all video stages, :196-224 maps them to <video preload='auto'>; NarrationLayer.tsx:104-113 maps NARRATED_IDS (=all 50, narration.ts:16) to <audio preload='auto'>; MediaLayer.tsx:92-96 (±2 display none)
  - **Verified:** CONFIRMED node count: parsed src/data/stages.ts — exactly 50 act2() stage instances inside the STAGES array, all video, zero non-video builders. narration.ts:16 NARRATED_IDS = STAGES.map(id) = all 50. So 50 <video preload='auto'> + 50 <audio preload='auto'> is accurate. Mitigations (display:none beyond ±2, src only near active, seek-throttle at MediaLayer.tsx:125-133) are real and reduce decode pressure, but the 100 retained media nodes with preload='auto' is the documented iOS risk. Major (medium confidence) is appropriate — device-perfect-on-every-screen is a signed-off requirement and iOS decoder exhaustion would break it.
- **T-F-04 - Add safe-area-inset padding to all bottom/side-pinned fixed UI (notch + home indicator)**  _(stage: responsive-allviewport - verified)_

  - **Evidence:** index.html:6 (viewport-fit=cover, verified); grep 'env(safe-area-inset' over src + index.html = 0 matches (verified, exit 1); grep 'env(' src | safe = 0.   - **Verified:** INDEPENDENTLY CONFIRMED. Re-grepped: viewport-fit=cover present (index.html:6), env(safe-area-inset = 0 hits across src and index.html, env( in src = 0. Every cited pinned position verified line-for-line. PlayButton.tsx:158-184 confirms .bar is the bottom-pinned fixed container holding Play + Speaker + Speed, so the control bar is genuinely affected. Because viewport-fit=cover explicitly disables auto-padding, overlap with the 34px home indicator is the documented failure mode. Major is correct: the primary playback control overlaps the home indicator. The user signed off 'perfect on EVERY screen size; broken/clipped/overflow layouts are real bugs', so this is in scope, not taste.
- **T-F-05 - Letterboxed clip is starved/collapsed on short landscape viewports (Voice on)**  _(stage: responsive-allviewport - verified)_
  - **Wrong:** On a short landscape phone the px-floored top offset plus the Voice-on caption-band reservation leave the Act-2 clip with near-zero height, so the clip effectively disappears.

  - **Evidence:** MediaLayer.module.css:25-29 (short/narrow query: top:max(20vh,210px); bottom:4vh), :40-44 (.withCaptions .stage bottom: clamp(8.5rem,16vh,11rem)). At 740x360 landscape the query matches (max-width:820 and max-height:600). top=max(72,210)=210px; Voice-on bottom=clamp floor 8.5rem=136px. Stage height = 360 - 210 - 136 = ~14px.

Recomputed for 740x360 Voice-on: stage height = 360 - 210 - 136 = +14px, NOT zero/negative as the finding states - but 14px for a contained 16:9 clip is functionally collapsed/invisible, so the breakage is real. There is no dedicated short-landscape height guard. ### MAJOR - I: Accessibility & ethics

- **T-I-03 - 'First EMG-to-text decoder' over-claims (Gaddy & Klein predate it)**  _(stage: accessibility-ethics - UNVERIFIED)_
  - **Wrong:** Foundation stage says 'the first EMG-to-text decoder ... came out of UC Davis.' Paper 3 itself cites Gaddy and Klein (2020, 2021) as prior 'EMG-to-speech benchmarks,' and the only 'first' the UC Davis papers actually claim is 'we further establish, for the first time, a quantitative relationship between EMG signals and S3 representations' — a much narrower claim. 'First EMG-to-text decoder' is not defensible as written and is exactly the kind of priority claim ASR experts will challenge.
  - **Fix:** Replace 'the first EMG-to-text decoder' with a defensible, scoped phrasing, e.g. 'the first non-invasive surface-EMG-to-text decoder built on these geometric features' or 'their alignment-free EMG-to-text decoder.' Mirror in narration + re-render captions/mp3.
  - **Accept:** No unscoped 'first EMG-to-text decoder' wording remains; the claim is bounded to non-invasive/surface-EMG + the geometric pipeline, consistent with Gaddy & Klein being cited as prior EMG-to-speech work in paper 3.
  - **Evidence:** stages.ts:419 sub and narration.json line 48 ('the first E M G to text decoder'); emg2speech p.2 'Unlike prior EMG-to-speech benchmarks (Gaddy and Klein, 2020, 2021)...'; emg2speech p.2 'we further establish, for the first time, a quantitative relationship between EMG signals and S3 representations' (the actual scoped 'first'). Paper 2 abstract frames the contribution as 'direct EMG-to-text translation ... at the phonemic level' — novel framing, not a global first.
  - **Verified:** _UNVERIFIED - adversarial verify was rate-limited; confirm against source before applying._
- **T-I-04 - Glowed white captions over video lack a contrast scrim (WCAG 1.4.3)**  _(stage: accessibility-ethics - UNVERIFIED)_
  - **Wrong:** The top-anchored Caption headline (.caption) over Act-2 Manim clips has only a white text-shadow glow and NO background scrim — unlike the subtitle band, which has a near-opaque rgba(8,8,9,0.92) scrim. Manim frames contain bright white strokes, labels and numbers; where white-on-dark line art puts a bright region behind the white glowed headline, contrast can fall below the 4.5:1 (or 3:1 large-text) AA threshold, and the glow actually reduces edge contrast rather than helping. The .ahead subtitle words use --ink-faint (#86857f) which the token comment claims '~4.6:1' against #050505 but is only borderline and not against bright video pixels.
  - **Fix:** Add a subtle radial/linear scrim behind the top caption block (and any caption that overlays the clip), matching the subtitle scrim approach (e.g., a .wrapTop .block::before gradient at ~0.55-0.85 opacity of --bg), or a backdrop blur + dim. Verify the glowed white headline maintains >=4.5:1 (>=3:1 for large text) against the brightest plausible frame behind it on representative stages (signal, every-pair-grid, arc).
  - **Accept:** Top caption text measures >=3:1 (large) / >=4.5:1 (normal) over the brightest frame of the clip behind it on at least signal, ctc, arc, and credits stages; .ahead subtitle words meet AA over the scrim. Checked with a contrast tool against captured frames.
  - **Evidence:** Caption.module.css:89-94 '.caption { color: var(--ink); text-shadow: var(--glow-text); }' (no background); MediaLayer.module.css only background is the layer base 'background: var(--bg)' (line 53), not behind the caption; contrast scrim exists only for subtitles (Subtitles.module.css:18-31 '.wrap::before ... rgba(8,8,9,0.92)'); tokens.css:15 '--ink-faint: #86857f' '~4.6:1' is measured vs the page bg, not vs video frames; tokens.css:24-25 glow shadows are white, which cannot raise contrast over white video content.
  - **Verified:** _UNVERIFIED - adversarial verify was rate-limited; confirm against source before applying._
- **T-I-05 - Alt is wrong about the mechanism ('pours') and omits every animated beat**  _(stage: distillation - verified)_
  - **Wrong:** The alt says the teacher lane 'pours knowledge into the bottom EMG lane projection' — but the scene uses dashed per-cell tie-lines + travelling pulse dots + a numeric gap readout that free-falls 1.00->0.04, not a pour. It also omits the entire lesson: the match-the-numbers ties, the dull-average trap, the contrastive claim-your-moment/push-rivals-away diagram, and the closing 0.5 L2 / 0.5 InfoNCE fork. A non-sighted user gets a wrong metaphor and none of the pedagogy.
  - **Fix:** Rewrite the alt to track the actual beats: face-to-face teacher/student vector columns; dashed ties pull the student to match and a gap readout falls 1.00 to 0.04; a flatten-to-gray detour warns against a dull average; a contrastive diagram pulls each moment to its partner and pushes rivals away; the two pulls meet under a fork labelled 0.5 L2 (copy the numbers) and 0.5 InfoNCE (keep each moment distinct).
  - **Accept:** Alt conveys the match pull, the trap, the contrastive pull, and the fork recipe so a non-sighted user learns the same lesson as a sighted viewer; it must not use 'pour' for a tie-line/gap mechanic.
  - **Evidence:** Scene beats: BEAT2-3 DashedLine ties + moving Dots (s16_distillation.py:135-166); BEAT4 dull-average smear (170-194); BEAT5 InfoNCE anchor/repel (196-238); BEAT6 fork '0.5 · L2'/'0.5 · InfoNCE' (253-276). Frame v_3.0 shows tie-lines + 'match the numbers' + gap 1.00; v_7.0 shows 'a dull average' + gap 0.34; v_end shows the fork with both pulls and gap 0.04. None of this is in the alt, which instead asserts a 'pour'.
  - **Verified:** Confirmed by reading the source beats and four frames: the on-screen mechanism is unambiguously dashed ties + a falling numeric gap, never a pour, and the alt mentions zero of the five animated beats. Major severity is correct — for screen-reader users the alt is the whole experience and here it is both inaccurate and near-empty of content.

The genuine, narrower defect: the flanks specifically read S-EH...L-Z, which echoes the decoy words "she sells ... shells" shown in the n-best list one beat earlier. A phonetics-literate viewer can read the edges as fragments of "sells", momentarily suggesting the example reuses that word rather than a clean unrelated context. It's a readability/consistency nit, not a factual contradiction: the narration never names "ocean" and the gap framing ("the sounds for ocean were never heard" / "not in any candidate") is correct.

The auditor's framing of an "internal contradiction" overstates it: the flanks are context phones by design (the GAP, not the flanks, carries ocean's missing sounds), and the narration never mentions "ocean", so there is no stated claim that the flanks are ocean's sounds. What remains provable is the cosmetic echo of the "sells/shells" decoys (frames bc_v_02 vs bc_v_05) — a minor readability nit for ARPAbet-literate viewers, not an accuracy error.
- **T-A-14 - "Distance falls to nothing" / counter to 0.0 overstates distillation success**  _(stage: copy-the-teacher - verified)_
  - **Wrong:** The pull beat shows the on-screen "distance to teacher" counter free-fall to 0.0 and the student line snap exactly onto the master curve, while narration says the student's "whole line slides onto the master's, and the distance between them falls to nothing." This depicts a PERFECT, zero-residual copy of the teacher. The report's central negative finding is that distillation does NOT close the gap at the word level (EMG-only 26.10 ≈ WavLM-distilled 26.14; audio crutch buys essentially nothing at word level; greedy PER pinned ~20.9%). So the absolute "falls to nothing"/0.0 reads as a results claim that contradicts the report.

  - **Accept:** The beat illustrates that distillation pulls the projection toward the teacher (the loss term) without an absolute zero-residual visual/wording that contradicts the report's EMG-only ≈ distilled word-level result.
  - **Evidence:** narration.json:28 "its whole line slides onto the master's, and the distance between them falls to nothing"; b12 lines 220-227: dist.animate.set_value(0.0) + student.set_points_smoothly(master_y); frame ctt_11.3_v.png shows readout "0.0" with the two lines fully merged. technical_report.md lines 137-139 and 189-191.
  - **Verified:** Science CONFIRMED verbatim against report lines 137-139 ("26.10 ≈ 26.14 ... audio crutch buys essentially nothing ... full-context encoder is what moves WER") and 189-191 (PER pinned ~20.9%). Visual CONFIRMED via frame ctt_11.3_v.png: readout 0.0 with student line snapped exactly onto master (code 223,227). I DOWNGRADED severity major->minor: (1) the beat legitimately illustrates the L2 distillation OBJECTIVE, not an end-to-end WER claim; (2) the auditor's proposed fix "add/keep a downstream beat noting 'sounding close' is imperfect" is ALREADY satisfied — the next two stages frozen-recognizer ("Copying the voice has a loophole") and blurry-average-cheat ("plant one point dead in the middle") explicitly undercut this beat on purpose, so the arc self-corrects within two stages. Residual issue is a localized wording/counter overstatement, not an uncorrected false results claim.

- **T-A-17 - Diagonal gloss "measure its own size" is loose for variance and risks reviving the dismissed loudness idea**  _(stage: every-pair-grid - verified)_
  - **Wrong:** Narration: "Down the diagonal a sensor meets itself, so those just measure its own size." The diagonal of a covariance matrix is variance (how much that one sensor's signal swings), not its "size." "Size" is vague and could be misread as amplitude/loudness — which two-sensors-dancing explicitly told viewers does NOT matter, risking reintroduction of the dismissed framing.
  - **Fix:** Reword to "so those just measure how much that one sensor swings on its own" (its own variance/activity), avoiding "size," which collides with the earlier loudness point.
  - **Accept:** Diagonal is described as a sensor's own variance/activity, with no wording that revives the dismissed loudness/amplitude framing.
  - **Evidence:** narration.json every-pair-grid: "...a sensor meets itself, so those just measure its own size." two-sensors-dancing narration: "this isn't about how loud either one is." technical_report.md line 61: SPD shrinkage covariance (diagonal = per-channel variance).
  - **Verified:** Confirmed: read two-sensors-dancing narration in full — it explicitly dismisses loudness ("this isn't about how loud either one is"). "Own size" is genuinely ambiguous toward amplitude. Minor is correct: it's a wording-precision risk, not a factual error (variance IS roughly per-sensor swing magnitude), and the diagonal label 'a sensor meets itself' on-screen is fine.

- **T-A-20 - "Four layers can no longer memorize" contradicts the project's own report**  _(stage: memorize-trap - verified)_
  - **Wrong:** Narration asserts shrinking to four layers means the model 'can no longer memorize.' The technical report states the 4-layer Conformer DOES memorize the 8,500 train sentences (train PER << val PER ~27%). conf_layers=4 is listed as a config, with generalization attributed to the full-context encoder and anti-overfit augmentation, not to four layers being incapable of memorizing. The absolute 'can no longer memorize' is an over-claim an ML reviewer would flag.
  - **Fix:** Soften to a capacity intuition, e.g. 'Keep the reader small, and there's far less room to memorize — it has to lean on the simple pattern instead.' Drop the absolute 'can no longer memorize.'
  - **Accept:** Narration no longer asserts a 4-layer net is incapable of memorizing; it reads as a capacity/regularization intuition consistent with the report (which says the 4-layer encoder does memorize the train set).
  - **Evidence:** narration.json key 'memorize-trap': 'Shrink the reader down to just four layers, and it can no longer memorize'. technical_report.md:204-205 ('the encoder memorizes the 8,500 train sentences (train PER << val PER ~27%)') and :105 (conf_layers=4 stated as config). Note stages.ts:280 uses the safer 'a giant model just memorizes' framing, so only narration over-claims.
  - **Verified:** Confirmed and slightly stronger than the auditor framed it: the report does not merely omit the claim, it directly contradicts it (line 204-205 says the 4-layer encoder memorizes the 8,500 train sentences). Minor is correct: it is an EXPLANATORY beat where intuition-first simplification is permitted, the on-screen 'memorize = wiggly curve through dots' sense differs from the report's 'low train PER' sense, and the fix is a one-phrase softening, not a headline-number error.
- **T-A-21 - Audit '= 0' reframes a leakage control as a hallucination-safety virtue**  _(stage: rerank - verified)_
  - **Wrong:** The on-screen 'verbatim-recall audit = 0 / never invents unsupported words' and narration 'it never writes a word the sounds don't support — zero times' drop the report's PRIMARY framing of this 0 (L169-170: 'no train-text leakage through the LLM' — the free reranker did not recover any reference ABSENT from the candidate set, i.e. it cannot conjure memorized train text) and recast it purely as acoustic grounding. The grounding gloss is not false, but it loses the leakage/memorization meaning and a reviewer reading Section 5.4 sees one number doing double duty.
  - **Fix:** Either (a) reframe to L169-170's meaning ('we checked it never just recites a memorized training sentence — recall of out-of-pool references is zero'), or (b) keep the grounding framing but let the binding-constraint stage immediately note this same 0 is why <10% WER is unreachable.
  - **Accept:** Audit-beat caption/sub/narration describe either the no-train-text-leakage finding or an honestly-bounded grounding claim traceable to report L169-170/L195-196, without implying a hallucination-proof safety property the report does not assert.
  - **Evidence:** scene s22_rerank.py L264,283-284 (label 'verbatim-recall audit', sub 'never invents unsupported words'); narration.json 'rerank' final sentence; report L169-170 'Free-generation recall of references absent from the candidate set = 0 (no train-text leakage through the LLM)'. Frame v_11.8.png confirms the on-screen text settling on 0.
  - **Verified:** DOWNGRADED major->minor. The grounding gloss is actually report-faithful: Section 5.4 L194-196 states the missing references are 'absent from the acoustic posteriors... there is no candidate' and that free generation to fix them 'would be hallucination (recall = 0 by audit)'. So the report ITSELF equates candidate-set absence with acoustic-posterior absence and presents recall=0 as a GOOD anti-hallucination property. The page picks one of the report's own two valid framings; it is a simplification that loses the leakage nuance, not a false 'negative-sold-as-positive' claim. Real but minor.
- **T-A-22 - Alt text 'small locked adapters' mislabels which QLoRA part is frozen**  _(stage: rerank - verified)_
  - **Wrong:** stages.ts alt says the model is 'squeezed to 4-bit with small locked adapters.' In QLoRA the 4-bit base weights are the frozen/locked part and the small LoRA adapters are the TRAINABLE part. Calling the adapters 'locked' inverts the mechanism.
  - **Fix:** Reword to 'squeezed to 4-bit with small trained adapters' or '4-bit base with small added adapters'.
  - **Accept:** Alt text no longer states the adapters are locked; freezing is attributed to the 4-bit base or the lock framing is dropped.
  - **Evidence:** stages.ts L381 'A 7-billion-parameter model squeezed to 4-bit with small locked adapters...'; report L160 'QLoRA (4-bit nf4 + LoRA r=16)'. LoRA adapters are the trained low-rank matrices; the base is frozen.
  - **Verified:** CONFIRMED. Verified stages.ts L381 verbatim and report L160. Standard QLoRA: 4-bit base frozen, LoRA adapters fine-tuned. The word 'locked' on 'adapters' is a genuine, provable inversion any LoRA-literate reader would flag. Minor is correct (alt text only, low audience reach).
- **T-A-23 - signal narration "thousands of points a second" is loose/ambiguous vs 5,000/s per channel**  _(stage: science-global - UNVERIFIED)_
  - **Wrong:** The signal narration first correctly says "five thousand times a second" (per channel), then later summarizes the 31 traces as "thousands of points a second." Per channel it is 5,000/s; across 31 channels it is ~155,000/s. "Thousands" understates the aggregate and is vague after the precise "five thousand" was just given. Minor since 5 kHz is stated correctly earlier, but the second phrasing reads as an inconsistency.
  - **Fix:** Make the aggregate explicit or drop it: e.g. "thirty-one wiggly lines, five thousand readings a second on each, overlapping" — keep the per-channel 5 kHz consistent.
  - **Accept:** The second mention no longer contradicts/under-counts the 5 kHz per-channel rate; phrasing is unambiguous.
  - **Evidence:** narration.json:7 (signal): "...taken five thousand times a second... thirty-one wiggly lines, thousands of points a second, overlapping...". Report Section 2: "31-channel surface array, 5 kHz" (per channel). stages.ts:169 sub avoids the issue ("five thousand times a second").
  - **Verified:** _UNVERIFIED - adversarial verify was rate-limited; confirm against source before applying._
- **T-A-24 - 'though' sound labelled 'OH' — not a valid ARPAbet symbol and inconsistent with the inventory's 'OW'**  _(stage: targets-phon - verified)_

The same vowel is taught as 'OH' then displayed as 'OW', undercutting the 'these are the fixed symbols' message for the ASR-literate audience.

Correcting severity major->minor: it is a single-glyph label fix that does not break the pipeline, mislead about the science, or damage the core 'same spelling, different sounds' point; it is a cosmetic/consistency defect, which is minor, not major.
- **T-A-25 - 'Linguists already counted these — about forty' conflates the ASR phoneme set with the linguistic phoneme count**  _(stage: targets-phon - verified)_
  - **Wrong:** The ~40 figure is the project's ARPAbet/CMU set (report 'phoneme (40+blank)'), an ASR convention; the standard linguistic count for General American English is ~44, and the displayed list includes 'AX' (schwa, absent from the canonical 39-phone CMUdict). Attributing the exact 'about forty' to 'linguists' is a soft over-simplification a phonetician could flag.
  - **Fix:** Soften to 'there's a small fixed set — about forty in the version we use' or 'roughly forty'.
  - **Accept:** Phoneme-count claim is hedged so it cannot be read as the exact linguistic inventory.
  - **Evidence:** narration.json: 'Linguists already counted these — about forty of them'; technical_report.md:65 'phoneme (40+blank)'; s10_targets_phon.py:201-206 lists 40 symbols including 'AX'.
  - **Verified:** Confirmed: report uses 40 as the ASR set; narration attributes 'about forty' to linguists; inventory includes AX. Real but soft; ethics/credit experts are not implicated, and 40 matches the report, so minor is appropriate (leans polish but stays minor).
- **T-A-26 - "thousands of hours" overstates HuBERT's training data (LibriSpeech 960h) — alt text only**  _(stage: targets-units - verified)_
  - **Wrong:** The alt text claims the 100 units were discovered from "thousands of hours of audio." The 100-unit HuBERT model (report cites Hsu et al. [7]) uses k-means clustering trained self-supervised on LibriSpeech 960h — just under one thousand hours. The fact sheet confirms 960h and flags 'thousands' as an overstatement. The technical report states no hours figure. So the science point is valid: "thousands" (implies >=2000) overstates ~960h.
  - **Fix:** Change both alt texts to "about a thousand hours of audio" (matches LibriSpeech 960h).
  - **Accept:** targets-units and where-units-from alt text state an hours figure consistent with HuBERT's actual training corpus (~960h ≈ "about a thousand hours"), not "thousands."
  - **Evidence:** stages.ts:226 (targets-units alt): "100 sound-shapes a model discovered on its own from thousands of hours of audio"; stages.ts:232 (where-units-from alt): "play a model thousands of hours of audio". technical_report.md line 65 cites HuBERT [7] with no hours figure. Fact sheet: HuBERT 100 units trained on LibriSpeech 960h.
  - **Verified:** Science CONFIRMED (960h vs 'thousands'). BUT the auditor's evidence is partly FABRICATED: it claims 'narration.json targets-units' contains the phrase. grep proves "thousands of hours" appears ZERO times in narration.json; the targets-units narration says only 'A separate model found them on its own' with no hours figure, and where-units-from narration says 'endless plain audio'. The phrase exists ONLY in the two alt-text strings (stages.ts:226, :232). Because it is alt-text-only (not spoken in TTS, not on-screen in the video), an 'ML reviewer will flag this' is overstated — alt text is screen-reader/SEO, far less scrutinized than narration. Severity corrected major->minor; narration citation removed from evidence.
- **T-A-27 - Covariance is wrongly framed as loudness-independent (it scales with amplitude)**  _(stage: two-sensors-dancing - verified)_
  - **Wrong:** The narration says "the second dancer is half as loud, yet the answer never changed... So this isn't about how loud either one is — it's purely the dance between them, and that single number is what we call covariance." Naming the loudness-invariant quantity "covariance" is statistically imprecise: covariance's MAGNITUDE scales directly with each signal's amplitude; only its SIGN (or the amplitude-normalized correlation) is loudness-invariant. The on-screen caption already says it correctly ("the SIGN is unchanged"), so the narration over-generalizes "sign" to "the answer/number itself."
  - **Fix:** Tie loudness-invariance to the SIGN/direction, not "the answer"/"the number." E.g. narration: "...yet the up-or-down verdict never changed — the SIGN of covariance gives the direction; only its size cares about loudness," and align the gloss accordingly.
  - **Accept:** No narration line claims covariance itself is loudness-independent; loudness-invariance is attributed only to the sign/direction (or renamed correlation); narration and the on-screen "SIGN is unchanged" wording agree.
  - **Evidence:** narration.json key two-sensors-dancing: "...half as loud, yet the answer never changed... this isn't about how loud either one is — it's purely the dance between them, and that single number is what we call covariance"; b01_two_sensors_dancing.py:248 on-screen caption correctly reads "B is half as loud as A — the SIGN is unchanged"; cov(a)=0.224 vs cov(0.5a)=0.112 confirms magnitude scales with amplitude; technical_report.md:61 names the feature "SPD shrinkage covariance."
  - **Verified:** Independently reproduced the scene's arrays: cov(1.0*a)=0.2237, cov(0.5*a)=0.1119 — magnitude halves with amplitude, so covariance is provably amplitude-dependent and the narration's framing is imprecise. SEVERITY CORRECTED major->minor: the on-screen caption (line 248) and slider already say the correct thing ("SIGN is unchanged"); the gloss "one number for how two move together" is defensible; the scene NEVER displays a full-loudness covariance, so the auditor's "+0.224 vs +0.112 spotlit" framing overstates it (B is half-loud the entire scene, displayed +0.11 throughout). It is a single fixable narration clause in an intuition beat, not a load-bearing pipeline number — minor, though a legitimate rigor flag for expert viewers.
- **T-A-28 - "thousands of hours" overstates HuBERT's training data (LibriSpeech 960h)**  _(stage: where-units-from - verified)_
  - **Wrong:** The on-screen waveform label and the stage sub/alt assert the model is fed 'thousands of hours' of audio. The 100-unit HuBERT clustering used here comes from HuBERT (Hsu et al., cited [7]) pretrained on LibriSpeech 960h — under one thousand hours. 'Thousands' (plural) overstates the true scale by ~2x. The fix is cheap and the core lesson (self-supervised on lots of unlabeled audio) is unaffected; the spoken narration already avoids the number, so only on-screen text + metadata are wrong. Hence minor, not major.
  - **Fix:** Change the on-screen label and the sub/alt to 'hundreds of hours of plain audio' or a non-numeric phrase ('a huge pile of plain audio — no labels'); keep visual, sub, and alt consistent with the spoken narration.
  - **Accept:** No on-screen text, sub, or alt claims 'thousands of hours'; the stated quantity is consistent with ~960h (e.g. 'hundreds of hours') or is non-numeric, matching the narration.
  - **Evidence:** b05_where_units_from.py:152 mono("thousands of hours of plain audio — no labels"); stages.ts:226 (targets-units neighbor) and :232 (this stage alt) both say 'thousands of hours of audio'. technical_report.md:65 'HuBERT-unit (100+blank) [7]' and :243 cite Hsu et al. HuBERT (LibriSpeech 960h via [10] Panayotov). narration.json 'where-units-from' uses 'endless plain audio — no labels, just sound' (no number).
  - **Verified:** Independently confirmed: b05:152 text and stages.ts:226/:232 verified by grep; report cites HuBERT [7] + LibriSpeech [10] with no hour count, and HuBERT-Base 100-unit clustering is LibriSpeech 960h (<1000h). Real overstatement. Downgraded major->minor because the audio (the most-consumed surface) is already clean, it is one imprecise word, and the ~2x error does not distort the pedagogy.

Frame at 5.8s shows the on-screen sub-caption "each asks: how relevant are you to me?" while the spoken "am I to you?" cue does not start until 11.16s.
  - **Verified:** The POV inversion across narration/scene/alt is REAL and verified. BUT the auditor's stated mechanism ("a careful viewer sees both simultaneously, reading as a contradiction") is INACCURATE: by frame timing the on-screen 'are you to me?' caption shows ~5-7s (beat 4) while the spoken 'am I to you?' subtitle runs 11.16-14.88s (beats 5-7), so they never co-occur on screen. The contradiction is sequential, not simultaneous. The defect itself (same question, opposite POV across the stage's text) still holds and minor severity is correct; I corrected the mechanism in evidence/verifyNote.

### MINOR - C: Narration quality

- **T-C-01 - On-screen weighted-sum tokens '0.5 · L2' and '0.5 · InfoNCE' read as a formula, against the no-on-screen-formula taste rule**  _(stage: distillation - verified)_
  - **Wrong:** The fork renders '0.5 · L2' and '0.5 · InfoNCE' as visible coefficient·name tokens. The signed-off taste decision is 'name the mechanics ... NO on-screen formulas'. The named mechanics (L2, InfoNCE) are fine and are define-after-show via 'copy the numbers' / 'keep each moment distinct', but the '0.5 ·' coefficient notation pushes the labels into weighted-sum-formula territory.
  - **Fix:** Drop the 0.5 coefficients and the '·' so the fork shows two equally-weighted named pulls ('L2 — copy the numbers' and 'InfoNCE — keep each moment distinct') without rendering a weighted sum.
  - **Accept:** On-screen text names the two pulls without rendering coefficient/weighted-sum notation, satisfying the no-on-screen-formula decision.
  - **Evidence:** s16_distillation.py:260-262 on-screen '0.5 · L2', '0.5 · InfoNCE'; both visible in frames v_11.5 and v_end. Taste decision: 'DEPTH: ... NO on-screen formulas.'
  - **Verified:** Confirmed the tokens render on screen (frames v_11.5, v_end). Kept at minor: it is a borderline taste-rule tension, not a science error; the names themselves are explicitly encouraged ('name distillation and what it optimizes') and are glossed in plain English, so only the bare '0.5 ·' coefficients are at issue.
- **T-C-02 - TTS pronunciation trap: phoneme symbol 'AE' voiced as letter names, not the /ae/ sound**  _(stage: targets-phon - verified)_
  - **Wrong:** Narration 'the sounds you actually make: K, AE, T.' The en-US-AvaMultilingualNeural voice reads 'AE' as the letter sequence (ay-ee), which does not convey the vowel in 'cat', contradicting 'the sounds you actually make'. K/T as letter names are tolerable; AE is the trap.
  - **Fix:** Gloss it for TTS, e.g. 'a K sound, the a-as-in-cat, a T sound', keeping the on-screen 'AE' glyph for the symbol. Per the VOICE taste rule, acronyms/codes must be spelled for TTS.
  - **Accept:** Spoken line conveys the actual sound; no raw phoneme code is voiced as ambiguous letters where a sound is implied.
  - **Evidence:** narration.json key targets-phon: '...the sounds you actually make: K, AE, T.'; targets-phon.captions.json beat-6 tokens 'K,' (21.898s) 'AE,' (22.739s) 'T.' (23.432s) — 'AE,' is a single token.
  - **Verified:** Confirmed via narration.json and captions.json: 'AE,' is one token at 22.739s. Directly violates the user-signed VOICE rule (spell acronyms for TTS). Minor is correct.
- **T-C-03 - Sub-line phrase "turns numbers in into a guess out" reads awkwardly**  _(stage: what-is-a-net - verified)_

Note the auditor's parenthetical that the scene "uses its own separate labels" is slightly inaccurate — the scene labels (b03 lines 9-10,119) are exactly "numbers in"/"a guess out", matching the sub — but this does not affect the core defect, which stands. Minor severity is correct: it is a readability nit on overlay text, not a comprehension blocker.

### MINOR - E: Pedagogy & completeness
