### MINOR - F: Code / UX / interaction

- **T-F-06 - Mandatory scroll-snap hook exists but is never mounted; docstrings contradict reality**  _(stage: code-ux - verified)_
  - **Wrong:** useScrollSnap.ts implements mandatory Lenis snap to every section but has zero call sites — StoryPage.tsx imports only useScrollProgress. useScrollSnap's docstring claims it is mounted on the Story route, directly contradicting StoryPage's docstring ('Scrolling is free (no mandatory snap) so the Act-2 clips can be scrubbed'). Mandatory snap would actively break mid-section scrubbing, so the dead hook is a trap.
  - **Fix:** Delete useScrollSnap.ts (dead code, F4) and remove the contradictory snap reference from any remaining docs.
  - **Accept:** No unused exported hook remains; remaining docstrings about snapping match actual behavior.
  - **Evidence:** grep 'useScrollSnap' src/ → only the definition at useScrollSnap.ts:24, no call site; StoryPage.tsx:10,22 (imports/calls only useScrollProgress); contradictory docstrings useScrollSnap.ts:21-23 vs StoryPage.tsx:16-18
  - **Verified:** CONFIRMED dead code: grep -rn useScrollSnap src/ returns ONLY useScrollSnap.ts:24 (the definition). StoryPage.tsx imports and calls useScrollProgress only (lines 10, 22). Docstring contradiction verified: useScrollSnap.ts:21-23 says 'Must be called... only where the story sections exist (the Story route)' while StoryPage.tsx:16-18 says 'Scrolling is free (no mandatory snap)'. Severity DOWNGRADED from major to minor: this is dead exported code (Clean Code F4) plus a doc contradiction — real and worth fixing, but there is no user-facing bug today (the hook never runs), so it does not rate major.
- **T-F-07 - Dead bottom-caption lift path: all 50 stages are captionPosition:'top', so .lifted never applies**  _(stage: code-ux - verified)_
  - **Wrong:** act2() hardcodes captionPosition:'top' (stages.ts:128) for every stage; there are zero bottom-position stages. In Caption.tsx atTop is therefore always true, so lifted = captionsMode && !atTop is always false (Caption.tsx:51). The .lifted CSS (Caption.module.css:16-18,53-55) and its branch are unreachable.
  - **Fix:** Remove the .lifted branch and its CSS (and the now-dead computation in Caption.tsx) unless a bottom stage is reintroduced.
  - **Accept:** No unreachable CSS class or JS branch tied to captionPosition:'bottom' remains unless a bottom stage actually exists; visual output unchanged.
  - **Evidence:** stages.ts:128 (captionPosition:'top' in the only stage builder act2); grep captionPosition → only :128 sets it, zero 'bottom'; Caption.tsx:46,51 (atTop always true → lifted always false); Caption.module.css:16-18,53-55 (.lifted)
  - **Verified:** CONFIRMED. grep captionPosition: only stages.ts:128 assigns it, value 'top', inside act2() which builds ALL 50 stages; node scan found 0 occurrences of captionPosition:'bottom'. Caption.tsx:46 atTop = (===''top') is therefore always true, making lifted (line 51) always false; Caption.module.css .lifted (16-18, 53-55) is dead. Minor (Clean Code G9 dead code) is correct.
- **T-F-08 - Subtitle scrim edge fade may leak a clip's bottom labels behind tall subtitles**  _(stage: code-ux - verified)_
  - **Wrong:** The scrim is a fixed pseudo-element inset:-1em -3.25em whose gradient fades to transparent in the top 15% and bottom 15% (percentages of the band). For a 5-line subtitle the band is tall, so each 15% transparent feather can approach ~0.75 line, through which a clip's own bottom-edge labels could remain faintly legible.
  - **Fix:** Make the opaque core a fixed-px band with only a small constant rem/px feather (not %), or measure subtitle height and raise the clip's bottom dynamically so the clip never overlaps the faded zone.
  - **Accept:** At 1/3/5 subtitle lines on portrait and landscape, no clip pixel/label is legible through the scrim behind any subtitle line; the feather is constant size regardless of line count.
  - **Evidence:** Subtitles.module.css:18-31 (percentage gradient stops 0%/15%/85%/100%, blur 7px); MediaLayer.module.css:37-39 (.withCaptions lift sized 'for the tallest subtitles ~4-5 lines')
  - **Verified:** PARTIALLY CONFIRMED, severity DOWNGRADED from major to minor. The current scrim is rgba(8,8,9,0.92) from 15% to 85% (a near-opaque core over 70% of the band) plus a 7px blur, and the code comment (Subtitles.module.css:15-17) explicitly targets 'even a tall 5-line subtitle over the clip's own bottom labels'. So the worst-case bleed is much milder than the finding implies. The residual risk is real (percentage-based feather grows with line count), but with 0.92 opacity + blur it is a faint edge artifact at most, not a legibility failure. Minor is the honest rating; medium confidence.
- **T-F-09 - Dev asset versioning uses Date.now() per module, splitting cache-busting across video/audio/captions**  _(stage: code-ux - verified)_
  - **Wrong:** In DEV, ASSET_VER = String(Date.now()) is evaluated once per module at import in three files, with a different timestamp each, then appended as ?v=. So the video, audio, and caption for the same stage get different ?v values and are cached independently; HMR re-imports can request the same asset under a new version. Prod uses __BUILD_ID__ (fine).
  - **Fix:** Compute one shared ASSET_VER in an assets util and import it in all three; keep prod __BUILD_ID__.
  - **Accept:** In dev, the same stage's mp4/mp3/captions share one ?v value; no duplicate fetches of the same asset under differing versions within a session.
  - **Evidence:** MediaLayer.tsx:29, NarrationLayer.tsx:23, Subtitles.tsx:15 (three separate `import.meta.env.DEV ? String(Date.now()) : __BUILD_ID__`)
  - **Verified:** CONFIRMED. Read all three files: MediaLayer.tsx:29, NarrationLayer.tsx:23, Subtitles.tsx:15 each independently compute ASSET_VER = import.meta.env.DEV ? String(Date.now()) : __BUILD_ID__. Three separate Date.now() evaluations at module load → different ?v per asset type for the same stage in dev. Dev-only impact, so minor is correct.
- **T-F-10 - Keyboard/focus gaps: rail jump doesn't move focus; captions hidden from AT; global Space double-fires; aria-label uses × glyph**  _(stage: code-ux - verified)_
  - **Wrong:** (a) ProgressRail.goto() scrolls but never moves focus, so keyboard users lose their place after a jump. (b) The live subtitle line is aria-hidden, so SR users get no spoken-word track. (c) PAUSE_KEYS includes ' ' on a window keydown listener, so Space while the Play button is focused both activates the button AND triggers the global pause. (d) Speed aria-label uses the × glyph.
  - **Fix:** After goto(), focus the target section (tabindex=-1 + focus). Expose captions to AT. Scope the Space/arrow handler to ignore events whose target is a button/input. Replace × with 'times' in aria-labels.
  - **Accept:** Activating a rail item moves focus to that stage; a screen reader announces the active sentence; Space on Play doesn't double-fire; aria-labels read 'two times'.
  - **Evidence:** ProgressRail.tsx:27-35 (no focus management after scrollTo); Subtitles.tsx:114 (aria-hidden='true'); PlayButton.tsx:27 (PAUSE_KEYS includes ' '), :142 (window keydown stop()); PlayButton.tsx:177 (`Playback speed ${speed}×`)
  - **Verified:** CONFIRMED all four sub-claims. ProgressRail.tsx:27-35 goto() does setPlaying(false)+lenis.scrollTo(el) with no focus move. Subtitles.tsx:114 wrap is aria-hidden='true'. PlayButton.tsx:27 PAUSE_KEYS = [...,' '] and :141-142 a window keydown calls stop() for any PAUSE_KEY while playing (target not filtered), so Space on the focused Play button fires both. PlayButton.tsx:177 aria-label uses literal '×'. WCAG-AA is signed-off; minor is correct for these cumulative gaps.
- **T-F-11 - Narration seeds currentTime from a NaN duration → press-Play-mid-stage starts voice at 0; caption fetch parse risk**  _(stage: code-ux - verified)_
  - **Wrong:** NarrationLayer seeds next.currentTime using next.duration, which is NaN until 'loadedmetadata'; it guards with Number.isFinite and falls back to 0 (NarrationLayer.tsx:72-74). So pressing Play mid-stage (or arming Voice mid-play) on a clip whose metadata hasn't loaded starts the voice at 0, contradicting the 'picks the voice up from that moment, like a video' docstring. Subtitles.load() also calls (await res.json()) on a 200 response, which logs a console error if the body is non-JSON.
  - **Fix:** Defer the narration seek until a one-shot 'loadedmetadata' listener fires, then seek to local*duration. For captions, await res.text() then JSON.parse inside try.
  - **Accept:** Pressing Play mid-stage starts the voice at the scroll-matched moment, not 0; no uncaught console error when a captions file is malformed or missing.
  - **Evidence:** NarrationLayer.tsx:72-74 (`const dur = next.duration; next.currentTime = ...Number.isFinite(dur) && dur>0 ? local*dur : 0`); NarrationLayer.tsx:61-62 docstring ('picks the voice up from that moment, like a video'); Subtitles.tsx:71-72 (res.ok ? (await res.json()).cues : [])
  - **Verified:** CONFIRMED the primary defect. NarrationLayer.tsx:72-74: dur=next.duration (NaN before loadedmetadata) → the ternary falls to 0. The clip switch happens the same tick the src is (re)set near the active stage (lines 54-56), so on first arm the metadata is typically not yet loaded and the voice starts at 0 — directly contradicting the lines 61-62 docstring. The caption json() parse risk (Subtitles.tsx:71-72) is real but lower-likelihood. Minor is correct.
- **T-F-12 - Reduced-motion users see a persistent 'scroll or press play' cue with no Play button and no narration/subtitles**  _(stage: code-ux - verified)_
  - **Wrong:** Under prefers-reduced-motion the play bar is display:none (PlayButton.module.css:114-118), so there is no Play, no narration, and no subtitles. MediaLayer forces the scroll-cue opacity to '1' when reduced (MediaLayer.tsx:177), and Caption renders the hero cue whenever !playing (always true for these users), so the text 'scroll or press play' stays fully lit forever even though there is no Play button to press — the instruction becomes a lie.
  - **Fix:** For reduced-motion change the cue text to 'scroll to begin' (no play affordance) and provide a captions/transcript surface; decouple subtitle visibility from the bar (ties to the DEFAULT-ON finding).
  - **Accept:** Reduced-motion users never see a 'press play' prompt with no Play button; they have a readable transcript/subtitle path.
  - **Evidence:** PlayButton.module.css:114-118 (.bar display:none for reduced-motion); MediaLayer.tsx:177 (cue opacity '1' when reduced); Caption.tsx:83-88 (hero cue shown while !playing); Caption.tsx:86 text 'scroll or press play'
  - **Verified:** CONFIRMED. PlayButton.module.css:114-118 hides .bar entirely under reduced-motion. MediaLayer.tsx:177 sets cue opacity '1' unconditionally when reduced. Caption.tsx:83-88 renders the cue (text 'scroll or press play', line 86) while !playing, which is permanently true for reduced-motion users since the only setPlaying(true) is in the now-hidden bar. So the cue is permanently lit and the 'press play' half is unactionable. Minor; the sr-only headings (StorySections.tsx:22-24) give a partial transcript, which is why this is not higher.
- **T-F-13 - ProgressRail rail-jump arms narration-gated subtitles inconsistently: clicking a stage never shows captions, but it also can't, because it force-stops Play**  _(stage: code-ux - verified)_
  - **Wrong:** ProgressRail.goto() calls setPlaying(false) before scrolling (to stop the auto-play loop overriding the jump), but it leaves narrationOn untouched. Because both NarrationLayer (shouldPlay = narrationOn && playing) and Subtitles (gated on narrationOn only) depend on these flags, a rail jump made while paused-with-voice-armed leaves narrationOn true and playing false: Subtitles will keep rendering the LAST clip's frozen caption band (Subtitles only early-returns when !on; narration.activeId is still set from the last play) until the next narration tick clears it. This is a subtle stale-caption flash on rail navigation while voice was armed.
  - **Fix:** In goto(), also clear the subtitle/narration band deterministically (e.g. set narration.activeId=null, or have Subtitles also gate on `playing`). Simplest: gate Subtitles render on narrationOn && playing to match NarrationLayer and Caption's captionsMode.
  - **Accept:** Clicking a progress-rail item while voice was armed never leaves a stale subtitle line from the previous stage on screen.
  - **Evidence:** ProgressRail.tsx:30-34 (setPlaying(false); lenis.scrollTo(el); narrationOn left as-is); NarrationLayer.tsx:49 (shouldPlay = narrationOn && playing → target becomes null when playing false, which DOES clear voiced on next tick), but Subtitles.tsx:110 gates only on `on=narrationOn`, and narration.activeId is only nulled once NarrationLayer's tick runs target!==voiced (NarrationLayer.tsx:63-69)
- **T-F-14 - Vestigial 3D scene machinery (SceneParams/sampleScene/stageIndexFor/OFF/A2/per-stage scene) is dead code after 3D removal**  _(stage: polish-assets - verified)_
  - **Wrong:** The live 3D Act-1 scene was removed (all 50 stages are act2/Manim), yet stages.ts still carries the full interpolation apparatus and the file docstring still claims 'Act 1 stages render the live 3D scene' (C2 obsolete comment). sampleScene/stageIndexFor are exported but never imported, so they are dead (G9) clutter (G12).
  - **Fix:** Confirm no live import remains (done — none), then delete SceneParams, Vec3, OFF, A2, lerp/lerpVec3/ease, sampleScene, stageIndexFor, drop the 'scene' field from Stage/act2, and trim the docstring to the Manim-only pipeline. Follow-up cleanup PR.
  - **Accept:** After removal the app still builds and renders; stages.ts no longer declares scene-interpolation types/functions; the docstring no longer references a live 3D Act-1 scene.
  - **Evidence:** stages.ts: SceneParams type (18+), OFF const (93), A2 const (102), function act2 (113) used for all 50 entries (grep ' act2(' = 50), sampleScene (462) and stageIndexFor (488) exported. grep across src for imports from stages shows only STAGES/stageMedia/stageScrollVh/STAGE_COUNT/Stage/StageMedia are imported — sampleScene/stageIndexFor are imported by NOTHING (the only other hits, useScrollProgress.ts:15-16, are inside a comment, not a call/import). Docstring lines 4-9 still describe a live 3D Act-1 scene.
  - **Verified:** Independently confirmed: all 50 STAGES are built via act2 (scene:A2 universally), and a src-wide grep proves sampleScene/stageIndexFor have zero importers (only mentioned in a comment in useScrollProgress.ts). The docstring at lines 4-9 is now factually false. Real dead code + obsolete comment. Severity minor upheld — it is non-shipping dead TS that doesn't affect runtime, appropriate as a follow-up cleanup.
- **T-F-15 - Control-bar and speaker buttons / volume thumb are small touch targets (WCAG citation overstated)**  _(stage: responsive-allviewport - verified)_
  - **Wrong:** The Play/Pause, Speed and Speaker buttons compute to ~29px tall with no min-height; the hover-revealed volume thumb is only 12px. Easy to mis-tap on coarse pointers, but the finding's WCAG-AA framing is wrong.
  - **Fix:** On @media (pointer:coarse) add min-height:44px to .btn/.speed/SpeakerControl .btn (and min-width:44px to the icon-only speaker toggle), keeping align-items:center; enlarge the range thumb to >=20px on coarse pointers.
  - **Accept:** On pointer:coarse devices every control in the fixed bottom bar measures >=44x44 CSS px while keeping the monochrome pill styling; the volume thumb is comfortably draggable.
  - **Evidence:** PlayButton.module.css:38-41 (.btn padding 0.5rem 1.1rem 0.5rem 0.95rem), :44-47 (.speed padding 0.5rem 0.85rem), :109-112 (line-height:1); font-size var(--t-label) floor 0.68rem (tokens.css:33). Computed: 0.5rem*2 (16px) + 0.68rem (10.88px) + 2px border = ~28.9px. SpeakerControl.module.css:15 (.btn padding 0.5rem 0.72rem), :99-103 (::-webkit/-moz thumb 12px). grep min-height|min-width|44px over story/*.css = 0 hits (verified).
  - **Verified:** CONFIRMED measurements and zero min-height, but DOWNGRADED major->minor because the WCAG claim is overstated. SC 2.5.5 (44px) is AAA, not AA. The applicable AA criterion is WCAG 2.2 SC 2.5.8 = 24px minimum; the ~29px buttons PASS it (verified by calc: 28.88 >= 24). So there is no WCAG AA failure for the pill buttons. The only sub-AA element is the 12px slider thumb, which is a hover/focus-revealed secondary control. Real usability polish, not a major a11y blocker; user's A11Y sign-off is WCAG AA, which the buttons meet.
- **T-F-16 - Subtitle scrim pseudo-element overflows the viewport edges on narrow phones**  _(stage: responsive-allviewport - verified)_
  - **Wrong:** At <600px the subtitle wrap is 92vw and its ::before scrim extends 3.25em beyond each horizontal edge, exceeding the available margin and overflowing the viewport; only body overflow-x:hidden hides the resulting horizontal scroll, clipping the blurred scrim to a hard edge.
  - **Fix:** Cap the wrap so the scrim fits: width: min(56ch, calc(100vw - 7em)); or constrain the scrim inset to max(-3.25em, calc(-1*(50vw - 50%))); simplest: <600px set width min(56ch,86vw) and reduce the scrim horizontal inset.
  - **Accept:** On 360-400px viewports the scrim's left/right edges sit inside the viewport (soft blur visible, not clipped to a hard line) and removing overflow-x:hidden produces no horizontal scrollbar for any subtitle length.
  - **Evidence:** Subtitles.module.css:9 (width min(56ch,90vw)), :56-57 (92vw @ <600px), :18-21 (::before inset -1em -3.25em on .wrap); globals.css:38 (overflow-x:hidden, verified). The scrim em is relative to inherited body font (--t-body floor 0.95rem; ~15.3px at 375px) since .wrap sets no font-size, so 3.25em ~= 49px per side, while 92vw of 375px leaves only ~15px margin per side.
  - **Verified:** CONFIRMED. All lines verified. The finding actually UNDERSTATES the overflow: it estimates 3.25em~26px, but the scrim em resolves against the inherited body font (~15.3px at 375px, since .wrap has no font-size), giving ~49px per side vs ~15px margin -> ~34px overflow each side, masked by globals.css:38 overflow-x:hidden. Real but cosmetic/latent; minor is correct.
- **T-F-17 - Hero two-line title reflows to 3-4 lines on the smallest phones (nav-collision claim unproven)**  _(stage: responsive-allviewport - verified)_
  - **Wrong:** The hero em-based max-width (14em) far exceeds available width on <=390px phones, so the title that is documented to stay a steady two lines actually wraps to 3-4 lines.
  - **Fix:** Clamp the em cap to the viewport: max-width: min(14em, calc(100vw - 2.5rem)); and/or lower --hero-big floor (~2.1rem) and reduce hero margin via @media (max-width:380px) so the title stays 2-3 lines.
  - **Accept:** On 320/360/390px portrait the hero occupies at most 3 lines, the two-line shape holds from ~390px up, and the title clears nav and control bar.
  - **Evidence:** Caption.module.css:101-105 (.hero .caption --hero-big clamp(2.5rem,...) ; font-size at landing hero-p=1 = --hero-big floor 2.5rem=40px; max-width:14em = 560px). On a 320px phone usable width ~295px << 560px, so the 14em cap never binds and the title wraps to many lines. The line-100 comment promises a steady TWO lines. Note .hero .caption (line 101) overrides the <600px .wrapTop .caption font reduction (line 44) by source order at equal specificity, so the big font persists on small screens.
  - **Verified:** PARTIALLY CONFIRMED, severity kept minor. The provable core is real: 14em (560px at the 2.5rem floor) exceeds small-viewport width, breaking the documented steady-two-line invariant on <=390px phones - verified against Caption.module.css:101-105 and tokens. HOWEVER the finding's nav-collision claim is UNPROVEN/overreaching: the hero renders in .wrapTop (Caption.tsx:57 atTop -> wrapTop), which is TOP-anchored (justify-content:flex-start, padding-top = nav-h + clamp; lines 23-25), so a tall title grows DOWNWARD away from the nav, not 'up under the fixed nav'. The genuine risk is the tall top band running into the Act-2 clip region, not nav overlap. Minor is correct; the layout-collision specifics are speculative and should be dropped from the writeup.

### MINOR - G: Consistency

- **T-G-06 - Typography drift: curly apostrophes/quotes among otherwise-straight glyphs**  _(stage: consistency - UNVERIFIED)_
  - **Wrong:** stages.ts uses straight ASCII apostrophes and quotes almost everywhere, but five strings slip in curly apostrophes (U+2019) and one slips in curly double quotes (U+201C/201D). Mixed glyph styles render inconsistently in the monochrome JetBrains Mono / Fraunces type and are a copy-paste tell.
  - **Fix:** Standardize on straight ASCII glyphs (the majority): replace the six curly occurrences with ' and \" . OR, if curly typography is the desired house style, convert ALL apostrophes/quotes to curly — but do not mix. Recommend straight ASCII since it is the established majority and avoids JSON-escaping pitfalls.
  - **Accept:** grep -P '[\x{2018}\x{2019}\x{201C}\x{201D}]' stages.ts returns nothing (or returns every apostrophe/quote in the file — fully consistent either way).
  - **Evidence:** Curly apostrophe U+2019 at stages.ts lines 155 ('What you’re about to learn.'), 286 ('one person’s data'), 411 ('What it’s for'), 413 ('microphone can’t'), 425 ('someone else’s work'). All other apostrophes (lines 188,208,218,244,256,278,280,290) and double quotes (lines 364,374) are straight ASCII.
  - **Verified:** _UNVERIFIED - adversarial verify was rate-limited; confirm against source before applying._

- **T-G-21 - The word "nudge" is overloaded across stages with several different meanings**  _(stage: what-is-a-net - verified)_
  - **Wrong:** "nudge" is reused for distinct technical operations: shrinkage of the covariance grid (features-embed), the forward-pass transformation of data through layers (what-is-a-net), and the gradient weight-update during training (how-training-works). Also found a FOURTH use the auditor missed: narration.json:40 ensemble-nbest "That nudges you from twenty-six percent wrong down to about twenty" (a WER improvement) — so the overload is broader than claimed. However I downgrade major->minor: "nudge" is a common informal verb and each instance is locally disambiguated by context ("toward a plain pattern", "at every dial", "in the direction that shrinks the error"); no reader is actually misled into a false mechanism, it is a clarity/polish concern not a correctness defect. The adjacency of what-is-a-net and how-training-works keeps it above polish.

## POLISH (60)

### POLISH - A: Scientific accuracy

- **T-A-29 - Animated meter uses un-squared average distance, which is flat along the segment (but invisible to viewers)**  _(stage: blurry-average-cheat - verified)_
  - **Wrong:** The narration's claim that minimizing closeness drives the student to the exact midpoint is correct for the real loss (squared L2, whose minimizer over two targets IS the midpoint). The animated meter, however, computes avg_dist=(d1+d2)/2 of un-squared norms, which is CONSTANT for every point on the segment between the two targets, so the displayed metric does not uniquely single out the midpoint. A pedantic ML viewer reasoning about the shown 'average distance' meter could note the midpoint is not uniquely optimal under it.
  - **Fix:** No narration change needed (L2 framing is correct). Optionally square the distances in avg_dist()/fill_width() so the midpoint is the genuine meter optimum. Keeping the student off-segment throughout the slide-in (already the case) means the meter improves monotonically and the defect never surfaces visually.
  - **Accept:** The visual incentive (meter) makes the midpoint the unique best point, consistent with the squared-error loss the narration abstracts; an ML reviewer cannot object that 'average distance is flat along the segment'.
  - **Evidence:** b14_blurry_average_cheat.py:121-124 avg_dist=(d1+d2)/2.0 (un-squared np.linalg.norm); lines 133-141 meter fill/brightness = f(avg_dist); narration.json:32 'Plant one point dead in the middle — equidistant'; technical_report.md:117 confirms the true term is '0.5·L2(proj, WavLM-L9)' (squared regression), whose mean is the unique minimizer — so the concept is sound, only the displayed meter is loose.
  - **Verified:** Math independently confirmed: for any point on the segment, d1+d2=|t1-t2| (constant), so avg_dist is flat — the finding is technically true. BUT the student slides directly from off-segment (s_mid reached via move_to from a point above, line 149/63) and never traverses the segment, so the meter visibly improves monotonically and the flatness is never shown. The auditor itself says 'no narration change needed' and rates it low confidence. Severity corrected from minor to POLISH: it is a real but viewer-invisible theoretical nitpick with no comprehension impact.

Downgraded from minor to POLISH: this is a soft illustrative-framing nuance, not a false numeric/mechanism claim, and the auditor self-rated confidence 'low'. Real but cosmetic.

- **T-D-35 - Title text renders as an illegible smear mid-morph during the qmark->title transform**  _(stage: second-opinion - verified)_
  - **Wrong:** At the start of beat 2 the title "two readers that fail differently" is created via ReplacementTransform from a single "?" glyph (b16 line 108-111). Because manim interpolates points between one glyph and a 28-character string, the intermediate state is a row of garbled/illegible blobs, not legible text. A viewer who scrubs and parks on that ~0.45s window sees nonsense where the title should be. Transient and resolves to crisp text, so polish severity.

  - **Accept:** At every scrub position the title is either absent or fully legible — no half-morphed or smeared glyph state appears.
  - **Evidence:** b16_second_opinion.py lines 107-111: title = mono("two readers that fail differently", ...); self.play(ReplacementTransform(qmark, title), run_time=0.45). Frame v_1.7.png (T=1.7s): title area is a row of fully illegible smeared blobs. Frame v_1.8.png (T=1.8s): partially formed garbled glyphs ('rcadcrs', 'diffcrcntly' artifacts). Frame v_5.0.png: crisp '...two readers that fail differently'.

### POLISH - F: Code / UX / interaction

- **T-F-18 - Four independent rAF loops scrub overlapping state; playSpeed doc says 1×–5× but SPEEDS tops out at 3×**  _(stage: code-ux - verified)_
  - **Wrong:** MediaLayer, NarrationLayer, Subtitles, and PlayButton each run their own requestAnimationFrame loop reacting to the same scroll/stage/narration state every frame — duplicated per-frame work. Separately, useStore documents playSpeed as '1×–5×' (useStore.ts:35) but SPEEDS = [1,1.5,2,3] (PlayButton.tsx:25) tops out at 3×, so the doc and the speed control disagree.
  - **Fix:** Fix the playSpeed comment to '1×–3×' (or extend SPEEDS to 5 to match — pick one). Optionally unify the per-frame ticks behind one shared rAF publisher, or document the duplication as intentional.
  - **Accept:** Docstring speed range matches SPEEDS; per-frame work is not triplicated/quadruplicated across loops (or the duplication is documented as intentional).
  - **Evidence:** PlayButton.tsx:110/131, NarrationLayer.tsx:93/95, Subtitles.tsx:101/103, MediaLayer.tsx:179/181 (four rAF loops); useStore.ts:35 ('1×–5×') vs PlayButton.tsx:25 (SPEEDS max 3)
  - **Verified:** CONFIRMED with a correction: grep shows FOUR rAF loops, not three — PlayButton, NarrationLayer, Subtitles, AND MediaLayer each requestAnimationFrame. useStore.ts:35 comment says '(1×–5×)'; PlayButton.tsx:25 SPEEDS=[1,1.5,2,3] caps at 3×. The doc/impl mismatch is real and trivially provable. Polish is correct.
- **T-F-19 - Subtitles `on` gate and Caption/MediaLayer `captionsMode` use different conditions (narrationOn vs narrationOn && playing), inviting a visible-subtitle-without-clip-lift state**  _(stage: code-ux - verified)_
  - **Wrong:** Subtitles render when `on = narrationOn` alone (Subtitles.tsx:49,110), but MediaLayer lifts the clip and Caption hides its sub only under `narrationOn && playing` (MediaLayer.tsx:69, Caption.tsx:50). So in any state where narrationOn is true but playing is false (e.g. just after a manual scroll pauses Play but leaves voice armed), Subtitles can paint into the bottom band while the clip has NOT been lifted to make room and the on-screen caption sub is still shown — producing the exact text-over-text / clip-over-subtitle overlap the lift was designed to prevent.
  - **Fix:** Make the three conditions identical — gate Subtitles on narrationOn && playing too — so the subtitle band only appears exactly when the clip is lifted and the duplicate sub is hidden.
  - **Accept:** There is no app state in which the subtitle band is visible while the clip is un-lifted or the caption sub is still shown.
  - **Evidence:** Subtitles.tsx:49 (on=narrationOn), :110 (return null only if !on); MediaLayer.tsx:69 (captionsMode = narrationOn && playing → lift gated on BOTH); Caption.tsx:50 (captionsMode = narrationOn && playing)
- **T-F-20 - ProgressRail tick (18px) and several glyph sizes are fixed px that don't track the fluid type scale**  _(stage: responsive-allviewport - verified)_
  - **Wrong:** Rail ticks, the play/pause/ff glyphs, and the volume thumb are fixed-px while all type uses clamp(); they look hairline on ultrawide and faint on tiny phones. Cosmetic, not clipping.
  - **Fix:** Express tick widths/glyph sizes with small clamp()/em values keyed to --t-label (e.g. tick width clamp(18px,1.4vw,26px)), or document the deliberate fixed-px choice. Lower priority than safe-area and tap-target items.
  - **Accept:** Rail ticks and control glyphs stay visually proportionate to surrounding fluid type from 320px to 2560px; no glyph becomes hairline-invisible on ultrawide or sub-perceptible on small phones.
  - **Evidence:** ProgressRail.module.css:28-37 (.tick width:18px height:1px), :58-61 (:hover 28px), :68-72 (.active 34px); PlayButton.module.css:69-107 (.play/.pause/.ff fixed-px borders); SpeakerControl.module.css:98-115 (thumb 12px). All verified.
  - **Verified:** CONFIRMED as polish. All cited px values verified line-for-line. This is a consistency/taste observation, not a breakage or overflow; the user's monochrome+fluid system makes it a legitimate but low-priority refinement. Correctly rated polish.

### POLISH - J: Polish

- **T-J-07 - Curly apostrophe in conformer alt breaks the straight-quote convention**  _(stage: conformer - verified)_
  - **Wrong:** The conformer alt text uses a curly apostrophe (U+2019) in 'one person's data', while this stage's own narration uses a straight ASCII apostrophe and the dominant convention across stages.ts is straight. One inconsistent character the consistency pass should normalize.
  - **Fix:** Replace the U+2019 in stages.ts L286 with a straight ASCII apostrophe to match the file's majority and this stage's narration (or normalize all 5 globally).
  - **Accept:** Apostrophe style in the conformer alt matches the narration for this stage and the dominant convention in stages.ts.
  - **Evidence:** hexdump of stages.ts L286 shows 'person' + e2 80 99 (U+2019) + 's data'; narration.json conformer key uses 0x27 straight 'person's'. Counts: 5 curly U+2019 vs 37 word-internal straight apostrophes in stages.ts.
  - **Verified:** Hexdump independently confirms e2 80 99 at the exact 'person<U+2019>s' position on L286; narration confirmed 0x27. Counts reproduced exactly (5 curly vs 37 straight). Real, provable, correctly rated polish.
- **T-J-08 - Scene header comments describe a 6-sentence script that no longer exists**  _(stage: end - verified)_
  - **Wrong:** s30_end.py lines 11-17 document "Six beats — one spoken sentence each" with six quoted narration lines, but narration.json end is only two sentences. The comment is stale documentation drift (Clean Code C2) that misleads future editors and likely caused the audio/visual length mismatch in Finding B.
  - **Fix:** Update the header to the real two-sentence narration, or drop the per-beat quoted script. Reconcile the six next_section beats with the two spoken sentences so the comment no longer asserts a false 1:1 mapping.
  - **Accept:** Scene comments accurately state current narration text and the real relationship between next_section beats and spoken sentences; no quoted comment line is absent from narration.json.
  - **Evidence:** s30_end.py:11-17 quotes six per-beat lines with durations 2.27/3.25/3.45/1.55/0.93/0.60 (= 12.05s); narration.json end = "From silent muscle to readable text — that was the whole idea. The end." (one 4.656s clip). Only "from silent muscle to readable text", "that was the whole idea", and "the end" survive as fragments; the other three quoted lines appear nowhere in narration.json.
  - **Verified:** Confirmed by reading both files. The six quoted lines and their per-beat durations summing to ~12.05s are in the header; narration.json end is two sentences (4.656s). Three of the six quoted lines (whisper of muscle turn into light / breaks apart scatter of tiny pieces / pieces find each other and become words) appear nowhere in the actual narration. Polish severity is correct: comment-only, no user-facing effect.
- **T-J-09 - Inconsistent period/quote placement between caption and sub of this stage**  _(stage: knobs - verified)_
  - **Wrong:** The caption puts the period INSIDE the closing quote ('I scream.') while the sub of the same stage puts it OUTSIDE ('I scream'.). Same phrase, two punctuation styles within one stage.
  - **Fix:** Pick one convention (US style: period inside the quote) and apply to both caption and sub.
  - **Accept:** Caption and sub use identical period/quote placement for the 'I scream' phrase.
  - **Evidence:** stages.ts line 356 (caption): "...or 'I scream.' Two dials..."; line 358 (sub): "...or 'I scream'. One dial...".
  - **Verified:** Confirmed by direct read of stages.ts lines 356 and 358: caption "'I scream.' Two dials" (period inside), sub "'I scream'. One dial" (period outside). Real and provable; polish severity is correct.
- **T-J-10 - distillation.poster.webp shows faint ghosted in-progress elements (clipped top header + half-drawn left boxes)**  _(stage: polish-assets - verified)_
  - **Wrong:** The distillation poster is legible and representative but is captured while two left-side boxes are still fading in (faint empty rectangles around an audio-waveform glyph) and a top header line is clipped at the very top edge.
  - **Fix:** Pick a slightly later timestamp where the left boxes are fully drawn or absent and the top header is complete or gone; re-export. Low priority.
  - **Accept:** No half-faded boxes or clipped top text in distillation.poster.webp.
  - **Evidence:** Direct frame read of public/anim/distillation.poster.webp: faint truncated text strip along the very top edge above 'teacher · layer 9'; faint partial rectangles on the left around a small waveform glyph. Core content (teacher·layer 9, 0.5·L2 / 0.5·InfoNCE, student·projection, gap 0.04) is fully legible.
  - **Verified:** Confirmed by viewing the image: faint ghosted left rectangles around a waveform and a clipped top text strip are both present. Severity polish upheld — frame is legible and on-brand; this is a cosmetic settle-frame nit, not a blocker.
- **T-J-11 - Posters hero/signal/ctc/conformer/heads/wfst/ensemble-nbest/foundation/end are clean and representative (informational)**  _(stage: polish-assets - verified)_
  - **Wrong:** No defect — recorded so these clean posters are not re-flagged.
  - **Fix:** No action.
  - **Accept:** n/a (informational).
  - **Evidence:** Verified foundation.poster.webp directly: legible, non-blank, on-brand monochrome full author card ('Harshavardhana T. Gowda, with Daniel C. Comstock & Lee M. Miller · University of California, Davis', 'our pipeline' block, geometric-perspective + emg2speech boxes). Consistent with the other named clean posters per the finding.
  - **Verified:** Spot-verified foundation.poster.webp is clean, legible, and on-brand as claimed. Note (out of polish-assets scope, flag for credit lens): the foundation card attributes 'a geometric perspective' to 'Gowda & Miller' only, but per the fact sheet McNaughton co-authored the SPD/geometry paper — a possible mis-attribution. That is a content/credit concern, not an asset-polish defect, so the polish positive stands. Informational positive confirmed.
- **T-J-12 - s_og.py social card is correct and on-brand (informational)**  _(stage: polish-assets - verified)_
  - **Wrong:** No defect — the Open Graph card is well-formed and consistent with the deck.
  - **Fix:** No action.
  - **Accept:** n/a (informational).
  - **Evidence:** s_og.py:11-41 — 1200x630 OG Scene; brand mono 'EMG → TEXT' (line 16); serif headline 'Reading speech from the / muscles of the face.' (18-20); num('18.5%',60,WHITE) (24) matching the 18.53 WER; mono label 'word error rate · surface EMG, no microphone' (26); sensor dots→arrow→'text' motif (32-36); uses serif/mono/num/glow helpers from emg_style; no color, no new typeface.
  - **Verified:** Read s_og.py directly; every claimed element is present at the cited lines. 18.5% matches the 18.53 WER ladder, 'no microphone' framing matches the deck, and only emg_style serif/mono helpers (Fraunces/JetBrains Mono) are used. Informational positive confirmed.
- **T-J-13 - Caption mis-attaches 'recorded only while training' to the model**  _(stage: voice-as-teacher - verified)_
  - **Wrong:** The caption 'Here the teacher is the real voice — a model that already learned to hear, recorded only while training.' places 'recorded only while training' adjacent to 'a model'. The closest antecedent is 'a model', but the audio model (WavLM) is pretrained and reused — it is the VOICE that was recorded only during training. A careful reader can misparse it as 'the model exists only during training.'
  - **Fix:** Reword e.g. 'Here the teacher is the real voice, captured only while training — read by a model that already learned to hear.'
  - **Accept:** The caption makes clear it is the recorded voice (not the audio model) that exists only during training.
  - **Evidence:** stages.ts:302 caption; the scene narration (narration.json key voice-as-teacher) correctly says 'while the muscle signal was being recorded, a microphone ran right beside the sensors, catching the real voice' — i.e. the voice is what was recorded.
  - **Verified:** Confirmed: the trailing modifier's nearest noun is 'a model', creating a genuine, if minor, ambiguity; the narration's phrasing shows the intended meaning attaches to the voice. Polish severity is correct (text clarity nit, no factual error).
- **T-J-14 - Caption/rail use straight double-quotes while apostrophes elsewhere are curly**  _(stage: what-is-a-net - verified)_
  - **Wrong:** This stage's rail title and caption use straight double-quotes, while apostrophes throughout the file are curly typographic ones and one closing card uses curly double-quotes — an inconsistent quote style on a page meant to be scrutinized.
  - **Fix:** Standardize all user-visible quoted text to one quote style (curly typographic recommended to match the existing curly apostrophes) and enforce consistently.
  - **Accept:** All user-visible quoted text uses one consistent quote style across the story.
  - **Evidence:** stages.ts:205 rail 'What "the model" is' and :206 caption '"the network reads it."' use straight double-quotes; stages.ts:430 uses curly “Thank you”; lines 155/286/411/413/425 use curly apostrophes.
  - **Verified:** Confirmed straight double-quotes at 205/206 and curly apostrophes at 155/286/411/413/425, plus curly double-quotes at 430 — so an inconsistency genuinely exists. IMPORTANT CORRECTION to the auditor's framing: across the whole file double-quotes are STRAIGHT on 4 lines (205,206,364,374) and CURLY on only 1 (430), so straight is actually the majority for double-quotes; only apostrophes are uniformly curly. The defect is therefore 'apostrophes curly but double-quotes mostly straight, with one stray curly double-quote' rather than 'this stage is the lone straight outlier'. Polish severity is correct.
- **T-J-15 - Caption 'Why this exists.' pairs incoherently with the mismatched sub**  _(stage: why - verified)_
  - **Wrong:** 'Why this exists.' is a fine rail headline, but with the current sub jumping to 'type by mouthing words' it reads as a non-sequitur. Once the sub is corrected per finding B, caption+sub should be re-read as one coherent thought.
  - **Fix:** After fixing the sub (finding B), re-read caption+sub together so they form a single coherent statement.
  - **Accept:** caption and sub read as one coherent statement about why the page exists.
  - **Evidence:** stages.ts lines 143-145: caption='Why this exists.' followed by sub that pivots to silent-mouthing, unrelated to 'why this exists'.
  - **Verified:** Confirmed as a real but trivial follow-on of finding B. It is purely contingent on B and adds no independent defect; polish is correct.
